202947_11_ITEM1_P0_S0	The Company was organized as a business corporation under the laws of Rhode Island in 1983 as Providence and Worcester Company and is the successor by merger in 1983 to a corporation also named Providence and Worcester Company which was organized under the laws of Delaware in 1979.
202947_11_ITEM1_P0_S1	In 1984, the Company s name was changed to Capital Properties, Inc.
202947_11_ITEM1_P1_S0	The current economic conditions have had limited impact on the Company s results of operations to date.
202947_11_ITEM1_P1_S1	In 2009, the Company granted rent concessions to two tenants of its leasing segment, which concessions terminated July 1, 2010, for a total increase of $93,000 annually.
202947_11_ITEM1_P1_S2	As none of the Company s leases require the tenant to provide financial information, the Company has no information concerning the impact of current economic conditions on its major tenants and, therefore, cannot predict whether any other tenants will request rent relief or concessions.
202947_11_ITEM1_P2_S0	The Company operates in two segments: leasing and petroleum storage.
202947_11_ITEM1_P2_S1	For financial information, see Note 9 of Notes to Consolidated Financial Statements in Item 8.
202947_11_ITEM1_P3_S0	The leasing segment is principally devoted to the leasing of Company-owned land in the Capital Center area ( Capital Center ) in downtown Providence, Rhode Island under long-term ground leases.
202947_11_ITEM1_P3_S1	The Company owns approximately 18 acres in the Capital Center consisting of 11 individual parcels.
202947_11_ITEM1_P4_S0	The Capital Center (approximately 77 acres of land) is the result of a development project undertaken by the State of Rhode Island, the City of Providence, the National Railroad Passenger Corporation ( Amtrak ) and the Company during the 1980 s in which two rivers, the Moshassuck and the Woonasquatucket, were moved, Amtrak s Northeast Corridor rail was relocated, a new railroad station (the Railroad Station ) was constructed and significant public improvements were made to improve pedestrian and vehicular traffic in the area.
202947_11_ITEM1_P5_S0	With the exception of the Steeple Street property, the Company has not acted, and does not intend to act, as a developer with respect to any improvements constructed on Company-owned parcels.
202947_11_ITEM1_P5_S1	Rather, the Company offers individual parcels for lease pursuant to long-term ground leases with terms of 99 years or more.
202947_11_ITEM1_P5_S2	Each lease contains provisions permitting the tenant to develop the parcel under certain terms and conditions.
202947_11_ITEM1_P5_S3	Each lease provides for periodic rent adjustments of various kinds.
202947_11_ITEM1_P6_S0	Each tenant is required to indemnify the Company with respect to all of the tenant s activities on the land.
202947_11_ITEM1_P6_S1	The leases contain other terms and conditions customary to such instruments.
202947_11_ITEM1_P7_S0	As part of the construction of the Railroad Station, the Federal Railroad Administration constructed a 330-car parking garage on the Company s land adjacent to the Railroad Station, and the Company paid one-half of the construction cost.
202947_11_ITEM1_P7_S1	Subsequently, the Company became the sole owner of the parking garage.
202947_11_ITEM1_P7_S2	In 2005, the Company sold the parking garage for $2,500,000 in cash and leased the underlying land to the buyer for 99 years at an initial annual contractual rental of $100,000.
202947_11_ITEM1_P7_S3	Under the lease the buyer is responsible for all real estate taxes and other expenses relating to the parking garage.
202947_11_ITEM1_P7_S4	The sale of the parking garage, while retaining title to the underlying land, is consistent with the Company s policy not to act as a developer with respect to improvements constructed on land that it currently owns or may hereafter acquire.
202947_11_ITEM1_P8_S0	The Company first began offering parcels for lease in the Capital Center area in the late 1980 s.
202947_11_ITEM1_P8_S1	As of December 31, 2010, six developed parcels have been leased by the Company under long-term leases of 99 years or more.

202947_11_ITEM1_P21_S0	The Company, through its wholly-owned subsidiary, Dunellen, LLC, owns a petroleum storage terminal with a capacity of approximately 1,000,000 barrels (the Terminal ) and the Wilkesbarre Pier (the Pier ), collectively referred to as the Facility, located in East Providence, Rhode Island.
202947_11_ITEM1_P21_S1	The Facility is leased to Global Companies, LLC ( Global ) for the storage and sale of petroleum distillates.
202947_11_ITEM1_P22_S0	The Terminal utilizes the Pier and pipelines connecting the Pier to the Terminal.
202947_11_ITEM1_P22_S1	The Company operates the Facility for Global pursuant to a contract with another Company subsidiary, Capital Terminal Company.
202947_11_ITEM1_P22_S2	The lease provides for a fixed monthly rent which is subject to annual cost-of-living adjustments.
202947_11_ITEM1_P22_S3	The lease expires April 30, 2013, but will continue thereafter on a year-to-year basis unless terminated by either party upon ninety days written notice.
202947_11_ITEM1_P22_S4	Global may terminate the lease on the anniversary date (April 30) provided it gives at least one year s written notice.
202947_11_ITEM1_P22_S5	The lease includes provisions for additional payments based upon petroleum throughput in any twelve-month period beginning on May 1 of each year and ending on April 30 of the subsequent year at the rate of $.10 per barrel for every barrel in excess of 4,000,000 barrels, and for real property taxes in excess of $106,000 annually.
202947_11_ITEM1_P22_S6	The Company bears all of the operating costs with respect to the Facility, including a portion of the real property taxes and insurance.
202947_11_ITEM1_P22_S7	In addition, Global has an option to purchase the Facility at any time during the term of the lease (other than the last year thereof) on the terms and conditions set forth in a separate option agreement.
202947_11_ITEM1_P22_S8	Under a companion agreement, Global has agreed to pay 50% of the cost of all improvements to the Pier but not more than $1,000,000; to date Global has paid $966,000.
202947_11_ITEM1_P23_S0	The operation of a petroleum storage facility carries with it the risk of environmental contamination.
202947_11_ITEM1_P24_S0	Environmental incident (2010): On August 30, 2010, during a regular facility inspection of the Terminal, a release of petroleum-contaminated water was discovered from the tank bottom of one of the Company s 150,000 barrel tanks (Tank 153).
202947_11_ITEM1_P24_S1	The Company notified the Rhode Island Department of Environmental Management (RIDEM), the Environmental Protection Agency and the United States Coast Guard.
202947_11_ITEM1_P24_S2	It also notified its insurance carriers of the release and the damage to the tank.
202947_11_ITEM1_P25_S0	The tank was emptied of product and the cleaning of the tank bottom was completed in September 2010.
202947_11_ITEM1_P25_S1	The petroleum-contaminated water released from the tank was contained on the secondary containment liner under the tank bottom, preventing contamination of the groundwater.
202947_11_ITEM1_P25_S2	The Company engaged an outside engineering firm to inspect the tank bottom to determine the cause and location of the release, as well as the extent of the required repairs.
202947_11_ITEM1_P25_S3	The findings of the inspection indicated that aggressive corrosion from inside the tank occurred, causing two holes in the immediate vicinity of the observed release, as well as several other holes or potential holes in other areas of the tank bottom.
202947_11_ITEM1_P25_S4	The report indicates that the corrosion was caused by microbial contamination, which was affirmed by a corrosion specialist.
202947_11_ITEM1_P26_S0	The total cost of the cleanup, inspection and repair of the tank was $550,000.
202947_11_ITEM1_P26_S1	Tank 153 was placed back in service in February 2011.
202947_11_ITEM1_P27_S0	The testing of certain of the Company s other tanks revealed the presence of corrosive microbial contaminants in Tanks 151 and 32.
202947_11_ITEM1_P27_S1	Both tanks were treated with a biocide and continue to be monitored and treated as necessary.
202947_11_ITEM1_P27_S2	Since Tank 32 had been inspected in June 2010, the Company believes that the contaminants have not affected the integrity of this tank bottom.
202947_11_ITEM1_P27_S3	However, since Tank 151 had not been inspected since construction in 2006, the Company took this tank out of service in the first quarter of 2011 for a complete inspection of the tank bottom.
202947_11_ITEM1_P28_S0	At this time, management does not know which costs, if any, will be recovered under its insurance policies; however, the Company has put its insurance carrier on notice under the property policy with its insurance carrier to recover the repair costs.
202947_11_ITEM1_P28_S1	The deductibles on the Company s insurance policies are $50,000 for environmental and $75,000 for property.
202947_11_ITEM1_P28_S2	In addition, the Company is reviewing all of the facts and circumstances to determine if it has a claim against third parties for costs of cleanup, inspection and repair.
202947_11_ITEM1_P28_S3	The Company cannot determine with any certainty what amount may be recovered from a third party and, accordingly, has not recorded any receivable at December 31, 2010.
202947_11_ITEM1_P29_S0	Environmental incident (2002): In 2002, during testing of monitoring wells at the Terminal, the Company s consulting engineer discovered free floating phase product in a groundwater monitoring well located on that portion of the Terminal purchased in 2000.
202947_11_ITEM1_P29_S1	Laboratory analysis indicated that the product was gasoline, which is not a product the Company ever stored at the Terminal.
202947_11_ITEM1_P29_S2	The Company commenced an environmental investigation and analysis, the results of which indicate that the gasoline did not come from the Terminal.
202947_11_ITEM1_P29_S3	RIDEM subsequently identified Power Test Realty Partnership (Power Test), the owner of an adjacent parcel, as a potentially responsible party for the contamination.
202947_11_ITEM1_P29_S4	Getty Properties Corp. is the general partner of Power Test.
202947_11_ITEM1_P30_S0	Power Test challenged that determination and, after an administrative hearing, on October 20, 2008, a RIDEM Hearing Officer determined that Power Test is responsible for the discharge of the petroleum product under the Rhode Island Oil Pollution Control Act, R.I.G.L. Section 46-12.5.1-3 and Rule 6(a) and 12(b) of the Oil Pollution Control Regulations.
202947_11_ITEM1_P30_S1	The RIDEM Decision and Order requires Power Test to remediate the contamination as directed by RIDEM and remanded the proposed penalty to RIDEM for recalculation.
202947_11_ITEM1_P30_S2	In November 2008, Power Test appealed the decision to the Rhode Island Superior Court.
202947_11_ITEM1_P30_S3	In addition, in November 2008, Power Test sought, and received, a stay of the Decision and Order of the Hearing Officer pending a clarification by RIDEM of the amount of the proposed penalty.
202947_11_ITEM1_P30_S4	On October 2, 2009, RIDEM issued a recalculated administrative penalty, and, subsequently, the RIDEM Hearing Officer issued a recommended amended decision, which was affirmed as a final decision by the RIDEM Director on December 23, 2009.
202947_11_ITEM1_P30_S5	On January 20, 2010, Power Test appealed that decision to Superior Court.
202947_11_ITEM1_P30_S6	There can be no assurance that the Superior Court will affirm the final RIDEM decision.
202947_11_ITEM1_P31_S0	In April 2009, the Company sued Power Test and Getty Properties Corp. in the Rhode Island Superior Court seeking remediation of the site or, in the alternative, the cost of the remediation.
202947_11_ITEM1_P31_S1	On May 1, 2009, Power Test and Getty Properties Corp. removed the action to the United States District Court for the District of Rhode Island.
202947_11_ITEM1_P32_S0	On May 22, 2009, Power Test and Getty Properties Corp. answered the Complaint and filed a Counterclaim against Dunellen, LLC and Capital Terminal Company alleging that Dunellen, LLC and Capital Terminal Company are responsible for the contamination.
202947_11_ITEM1_P32_S1	Getty Properties Corp. and Power Test have joined Getty Petroleum Marketing, Inc., the tenant under a long-term lease with Getty Properties Corp. of the adjacent property, as a defendant.
202947_11_ITEM1_P32_S2	The Company has amended its Complaint to add Getty Petroleum Marketing, Inc. as a defendant.
202947_11_ITEM1_P33_S0	In February 2011, the Company was notified by the United States District Court for the District of Rhode Island that the case was being transferred to the United States District Court for the District of New Hampshire due to a backlog of cases in Rhode Island.
202947_11_ITEM1_P34_S0	The parties are now engaged in discovery.
202947_11_ITEM1_P34_S1	There can be no assurance that the Company will prevail in this litigation.
202947_11_ITEM1_P35_S0	Since January 2003, the Company has not incurred significant costs in connection with this matter, other than ongoing litigation costs, and is unable to determine the costs it might incur to remedy the situation, as well as any costs to investigate, defend and seek reimbursement from the responsible party with respect to this contamination.
202947_11_ITEM1_P35_S1	This situation does not affect current operations at the Facility but may affect the Company s ability to sell the Facility should it determine to do so.
202947_11_ITEM1_P36_S0	In 1994, a leak was discovered in a 25,000 barrel storage tank at the Terminal which allowed the escape of a small amount of fuel oil.
202947_11_ITEM1_P36_S1	All required notices were made to RIDEM.
202947_11_ITEM1_P36_S2	In 2000, the tank was demolished and testing of the groundwater indicated that there was no large pooling of contaminants.
202947_11_ITEM1_P37_S0	In 2001, RIDEM approved a plan pursuant to which the Company installed a passive system consisting of three wells and commenced monitoring the wells.
202947_11_ITEM1_P38_S0	In 2003, RIDEM decided that the passive monitoring system previously approved was not sufficient and required the Company to design an active remediation system for the removal of product from the contaminated site.
202947_11_ITEM1_P38_S1	The Company and its consulting engineers began the pre-design testing of the site in the fourth quarter of 2004.
202947_11_ITEM1_P38_S2	The consulting engineers estimated a total cost of $200,000 to design, install and operate the system, which amount was accrued in 2004.
202947_11_ITEM1_P39_S0	RIDEM has not taken any action on the Company s proposed plan.
202947_11_ITEM1_P40_S0	As designed, the system will pump out the contaminants which will be disposed of in compliance with applicable regulations.
202947_11_ITEM1_P40_S1	After a period of time, the groundwater will be tested to determine if sufficient contaminants have been removed.
202947_11_ITEM1_P40_S2	While the Company and its consulting engineers believe that the proposed active remediation system will correct the situation, it is possible that RIDEM could require the Company to expand remediation efforts, which could result in the Company incurring additional costs.
202947_11_ITEM1_P41_S0	The Company manages its exposure to contamination, remediation or similar costs associated with the Facility through adherence to established procedures for operations and equipment maintenance.
202947_11_ITEM1_P42_S0	The Company maintains what management believes to be adequate levels of insurance, including environmental insurance.
202947_11_ITEM1_P43_S0	The Company notified its insurance company of the gasoline contamination associated with the incident in 2002.
202947_11_ITEM1_P43_S1	The insurance company advised the Company that coverage is only provided under policies in place at the time the contamination occurs.
202947_11_ITEM1_P44_S0	The Facility competes with several other similar facilities located on and adjacent to the Providence Harbor.
202947_11_ITEM1_P45_S0	The Terminal has approximately 42% of the total distillate storage capacity in the Providence area.
202947_11_ITEM1_P46_S0	Global competes with other terminal operators on the basis of price, availability, and a willingness to advance credit to local wholesalers.
202947_11_ITEM1_P46_S1	The amount of petroleum throughput at the Terminal is a function of Global s ability to compete effectively in the marketplace.
202947_11_ITEM1_P47_S0	The Terminal employs seven people on a full-time basis and one person on a part-time basis.

202947_11_ITEM7_P0_S0	The Securities and Exchange Commission ( SEC ) has issued guidance for the disclosure of critical accounting policies.
202947_11_ITEM7_P0_S1	The SEC defines such policies as those that require application of management s most difficult, subjective or complex judgments, often as a result of the need to make estimates about the effect of matters that are inherently uncertain and may change in subsequent periods.
202947_11_ITEM7_P1_S0	The Company s significant accounting policies are described in Note 2 of Notes to Consolidated Financial Statements in Item 8.
202947_11_ITEM7_P1_S1	Not all of these significant accounting policies require management to make difficult, subjective or complex judgments or estimates.
202947_11_ITEM7_P1_S2	Management believes that the Company s revenue recognition policy for long-term leases with scheduled rent increases (leasing segment) meets the SEC definition of critical.
202947_11_ITEM7_P2_S0	Certain of the Company s long-term land leases have original terms of 30 to 149 years and contain scheduled rent increases where the future dollar increases are known at the time of the commencement of the lease or at a subsequent date.
202947_11_ITEM7_P3_S0	The first such lease commenced in 1988, had an original term of 99 years and provides for fixed percentage increases at specified intervals (as well as reappraisal increases).
202947_11_ITEM7_P3_S1	In accordance with United States generally accepted accounting principles in accounting for leases, rental income related to the fixed percentage increases that are presently known should be recognized on a straight-line basis.
202947_11_ITEM7_P3_S2	To calculate the annual straight-line amount, the 99 known annual rental amounts are totaled and this total is divided by 99.
202947_11_ITEM7_P4_S0	In 2009, a scheduled appraisal occurred, resulting in a rental increase.
202947_11_ITEM7_P4_S1	The Company recalculated the future annual straight-line amount using the remaining years under the lease.
202947_11_ITEM7_P4_S2	The turnaround date discussed below did not change.
202947_11_ITEM7_P5_S0	For this lease, the calculated annual straight-line amount for 1988 was eight times (multiple) the amount paid by the tenant under the terms of the lease (the contractual amount ).
202947_11_ITEM7_P5_S1	In subsequent years, as the tenant pays higher rents, the multiple gradually decreases until the 57 th year of the lease, at which time the contractual amount paid by the tenant will exceed the calculated straight-line amount.
202947_11_ITEM7_P5_S2	If the Company were to report annual revenue for this lease using the straight-line amount, it would record a significant receivable for each of the first 56 years, which receivable would grow to approximately $34,000,000.
202947_11_ITEM7_P5_S3	Management does not believe that the Company should record a receivable that would not begin to be collected until the 56 th year (the turnaround date ) since management could not be assured of collection.
202947_11_ITEM7_P6_S0	In 1988, management met with the SEC accounting staff to discuss its concerns in applying United States generally accepted accounting principles as they related to a lease of this length which results in the recording of such a significant receivable that would remain on the Company s balance sheet and continue to grow on an annual basis with a turnaround date so far in the future.
202947_11_ITEM7_P6_S1	The Company presented the SEC accounting staff with an application of the accounting policy whereby management would evaluate the collectibility of the receivable on an annual basis and report as leasing revenue only that portion of the receivable that management could presently conclude would be collectible.
202947_11_ITEM7_P6_S2	The SEC accounting staff did not object to this application by the Company.
202947_11_ITEM7_P7_S0	Through December 31, 2010, the receivable on this lease has grown to $19,290,000 (cumulative excess of straight-line over contractual rentals) and management has not been able to conclude that any portion is collectible as the turnaround date is still 35 years away.
202947_11_ITEM7_P8_S0	In 2004, a second such lease commenced with an original term of 149 years and provides for fixed minimum percentage increases at specified intervals (as well as reappraisal increases).
202947_11_ITEM7_P8_S1	For this lease, the contractual amount paid by the tenant will not exceed the calculated straight-line amount until the 94 th year of the lease.
202947_11_ITEM7_P8_S2	Through December 31, 2010, the receivable on this lease is $16,019,000 (cumulative excess of straight-line over contractual rentals) and management has not been able to conclude that any portion is collectible as the turnaround date is 87 years away.
202947_11_ITEM7_P9_S0	In 2006, the Company entered into an Amended and Restated Agreement of its lease with Lamar Outdoor Advertising LLC ( Lamar ) with a current remaining term of 25 years which provides for fixed percentage increases annually.
202947_11_ITEM7_P9_S1	For this lease, the contractual amount paid by Lamar will not exceed the calculated straight-line amount until the 16 th year of the lease.
202947_11_ITEM7_P9_S2	Through December 31, 2010, the receivable on this lease is $1,021,000 (cumulative excess of straight-line over contractual rentals) and management has not been able to conclude that any portion is collectible as the turnaround date is 11 years away.
202947_11_ITEM7_P10_S0	Accordingly, the Company has not reported any portion of these amounts as leasing revenue in its consolidated financial statements and does not anticipate that it can reach such a conclusion until the turnaround dates are closer.
202947_11_ITEM7_P11_S0	Although the Company s other long-term land leases provide for scheduled rent increases, the provisions of the leases are such that certain future dollar amounts could not be calculated either at the time of the commencement of the lease or now, as such amounts are based on factors that are not presently known, i.e., future cost-of -living adjustments or future appraised values.
202947_11_ITEM7_P11_S1	Through December 31, 2010, the receivable on these leases is $8,820,000 and management has not been able to conclude that any portion is collectible as the turnaround dates are approximately 50 years away.
202947_11_ITEM7_P12_S0	The Company continues to recognize accrued leasing revenue from two leases which were recorded in prior years.
202947_11_ITEM7_P13_S0	The Company operates in two segments: leasing and petroleum storage.
202947_11_ITEM7_P14_S0	The leasing segment consists of the long-term leasing of certain of its real estate interests in downtown Providence, Rhode Island (upon the commencement of which the tenants have been required to construct buildings thereon, with the exception of a parking garage), the leasing of a portion of the Steeple Street Building acquired in 2007 under short-term leasing arrangements and the leasing of locations along interstate and primary highways in Rhode Island and Massachusetts to Lamar which has constructed outdoor advertising boards thereon.
202947_11_ITEM7_P14_S1	The Company anticipates that the future development of its remaining properties in and adjacent to the Capital Center area will consist primarily of long-term ground leases.
202947_11_ITEM7_P14_S2	Pending this development, the Company leases these parcels for public parking under short-term leasing arrangements to Metropark.
202947_11_ITEM7_P15_S0	The petroleum storage segment consists of operating the Facility in East Providence, Rhode Island, for Global Companies, LLC ( Global ).
202947_11_ITEM7_P16_S0	The principal difference between the two segments relates to the nature of the operations.

202947_11_ITEM7_P36_S0	On August 30, 2010, during a regular facility inspection of the Terminal, a release of petroleum-contaminated water was discovered from the tank bottom of one of the Company s 150,000 barrel tanks (Tank 153).
202947_11_ITEM7_P36_S1	The Company notified the Rhode Island Department of Environmental Management (RIDEM), the Environmental Protection Agency and the United States Coast Guard.
202947_11_ITEM7_P36_S2	It also notified its insurance carriers of the release and the damage to the tank.
202947_11_ITEM7_P37_S0	The tank was emptied of product and the cleaning of the tank bottom was completed in September.
202947_11_ITEM7_P37_S1	The petroleum-contaminated water released from the tank was contained on the secondary containment liner under the tank bottom, preventing contamination of the groundwater.
202947_11_ITEM7_P37_S2	The Company engaged an outside engineering firm to inspect the tank bottom to determine the cause and location of the release, as well as the extent of the required repairs.
202947_11_ITEM7_P37_S3	The findings of the inspection indicated that aggressive corrosion from inside the tank occurred, causing two holes in the immediate vicinity of the observed release, as well as several other holes or potential holes in other areas of the tank bottom.
202947_11_ITEM7_P37_S4	The report indicates that the corrosion was caused by microbial contamination, which was affirmed by a corrosion specialist.
202947_11_ITEM7_P38_S0	The total cost of the cleanup, inspection and repair of the tank was $550,000 (of which $273,000 has been paid through December 31, 2010).
202947_11_ITEM7_P38_S1	The tank was placed back in service in February 2011.
202947_11_ITEM7_P39_S0	The testing of certain of the Company s other tanks revealed the presence of corrosive microbial contaminants in Tanks 151 and 32.
202947_11_ITEM7_P39_S1	Both tanks were treated with a biocide and continue to be monitored and treated as necessary.
202947_11_ITEM7_P39_S2	Since Tank 32 had been inspected in June 2010, the Company believes that the contaminants have not affected the integrity of this tank bottom.
202947_11_ITEM7_P39_S3	However, since Tank 151 had not been inspected since construction in 2006, the Company took this tank out of service in February 2011 for approximately one month for a complete inspection of the tank bottom.
202947_11_ITEM7_P40_S0	At this time, management does not know which costs, if any, will be recovered under its insurance policies; however, the Company has put its insurance carrier on notice under the property policy with its insurance carrier to recover the repair costs.
202947_11_ITEM7_P40_S1	The deductibles on the Company s insurance policies are $50,000 for environmental and $75,000 for property.
202947_11_ITEM7_P40_S2	In addition, the Company is reviewing all of the facts and circumstances to determine if it has a claim against third parties for costs of cleanup, inspection and repair.
202947_11_ITEM7_P40_S3	The Company cannot determine with any certainty what amount may be recovered from a third party and, accordingly, has not recorded any receivable at December 31, 2010.

202947_11_ITEM7_P41_S1	The declaration of future dividends and the amount thereof will depend on the Company s future earnings, financial factors and other events.

202947_11_ITEM8_P16_S0	The Company follows United States generally accepted accounting principles when accounting for the impairment or disposal of long-lived assets, which requires that properties and equipment held and used by the Company be reviewed for impairment whenever events or changes in circumstances indicate that the net book value of the asset may not be recoverable.
202947_11_ITEM8_P16_S1	An impairment loss will be recognized if the sum of the expected future cash flows (undiscounted and before interest) from the use of the asset is less than the net book value of the asset.
202947_11_ITEM8_P16_S2	Generally, the amount of the impairment loss is measured as the difference between the net book value and the estimated fair value of the asset.

202947_11_ITEM8_P52_S1	Under a companion agreement, Global agreed to make certain improvements at the Pier which totaled $77,000 in 2010.
202947_11_ITEM8_P52_S2	No improvements were made in 2009.
202947_11_ITEM8_P53_S0	On August 30, 2010, during a regular facility inspection of the Terminal, a release of petroleum-contaminated water was discovered from the tank bottom of one of the Company s 150,000 barrel tanks (Tank 153).
202947_11_ITEM8_P53_S1	The Company notified the Rhode Island Department of Environmental Management (RIDEM), the Environmental Protection Agency and the United States Coast Guard.
202947_11_ITEM8_P53_S2	It also notified its insurance carriers of the release and the damage to the tank.
202947_11_ITEM8_P54_S0	The tank was emptied of product and the cleaning of the tank bottom was completed by September 11, 2010.
202947_11_ITEM8_P54_S1	The petroleum-contaminated water released from the tank was contained on the secondary containment liner under the tank bottom, preventing contamination of the groundwater.
202947_11_ITEM8_P54_S2	The Company engaged an outside engineering firm to inspect the tank bottom to determine the cause and location of the release, as well as the extent of the required repairs.
202947_11_ITEM8_P54_S3	The findings of the inspection indicated that aggressive corrosion from inside the tank occurred, causing two holes in the immediate vicinity of the observed release, as well as several other holes or potential holes in other areas of the tank bottom.
202947_11_ITEM8_P54_S4	The report indicates that the corrosion was caused by microbial contamination, which was affirmed by a corrosion specialist.
202947_11_ITEM8_P55_S0	The total cost of the cleanup, inspection and repair of the tank was $550,000 (of which $273,000 has been paid through December 31, 2010), which amount is included in petroleum storage facility expenses on the accompanying consolidated statement of income and retained earnings for the year ended December 31, 2010.
202947_11_ITEM8_P55_S1	The tank was placed back in service in February 2011.
202947_11_ITEM8_P56_S0	The testing of certain of the Company s other tanks revealed the presence of corrosive microbial contaminants in Tanks 151 and 32.
202947_11_ITEM8_P56_S1	Both tanks were treated with a biocide and continue to be monitored and treated as necessary.
202947_11_ITEM8_P56_S2	Since Tank 32 had been inspected in June 2010, the Company believes that the contaminants have not affected the integrity of this tank bottom.
202947_11_ITEM8_P56_S3	However, since Tank 151 had not been inspected since construction in 2006, the Company took this tank out of service in February 2011 for approximately one month for a complete inspection of the tank bottom.
202947_11_ITEM8_P57_S0	At this time, management does not know which costs, if any, will be recovered under its insurance policies; however, the Company has put its insurance carrier on notice under the property policy with its insurance carrier to recover the repair costs.
202947_11_ITEM8_P57_S1	The deductibles on the Company s insurance policies are $50,000 for environmental and $75,000 for property.
202947_11_ITEM8_P57_S2	In addition, the Company is reviewing all of the facts and circumstances to determine if it has a claim against third parties for costs of cleanup, inspection and repair.
202947_11_ITEM8_P57_S3	The Company cannot determine with any certainty what amount may be recovered from a third party and, accordingly, has not recorded any receivable at December 31, 2010.
202947_11_ITEM8_P58_S0	In 2002, during testing of monitoring wells at the Terminal, the Company s consulting engineer discovered free floating phase product in a groundwater monitoring well located on that portion of the Terminal purchased in 2000.
202947_11_ITEM8_P58_S1	Laboratory analysis indicated that the product was gasoline, which is not a product the Company ever stored at the Terminal.
202947_11_ITEM8_P58_S2	The Company commenced an environmental investigation and analysis, the results of which indicate that the gasoline did not come from the Terminal.
202947_11_ITEM8_P58_S3	RIDEM subsequently identified Power Test Realty Partnership (Power Test), the owner of an adjacent parcel, as a potentially responsible party for the contamination.
202947_11_ITEM8_P58_S4	Getty Properties Corp. is the general partner of Power Test.
202947_11_ITEM8_P59_S0	Power Test challenged that determination and, after an administrative hearing, on October 20, 2008, a RIDEM Hearing Officer determined that Power Test is responsible for the discharge of the petroleum product under the Rhode Island Oil Pollution Control Act, R.I.G.L. Section 46-12.5.1-3 and Rule 6(a) and 12(b) of the Oil Pollution Control Regulations.
202947_11_ITEM8_P59_S1	The RIDEM Decision and Order requires Power Test to remediate the contamination as directed by RIDEM and remanded the proposed penalty to RIDEM for recalculation.
202947_11_ITEM8_P59_S2	In November 2008, Power Test appealed the decision to the Rhode Island Superior Court.
202947_11_ITEM8_P59_S3	In addition, in November 2008, Power Test sought, and received, a stay of the Decision and Order of the Hearing Officer pending a clarification by RIDEM of the amount of the proposed penalty.
202947_11_ITEM8_P59_S4	On October 2, 2009, RIDEM issued a recalculated administrative penalty, and, subsequently, the RIDEM Hearing Officer issued a recommended amended decision, which was affirmed as a final decision by the RIDEM Director on December 23, 2009.
202947_11_ITEM8_P59_S5	On January 20, 2010, Power Test appealed that decision to Superior Court.
202947_11_ITEM8_P59_S6	There can be no assurance that the Superior Court will affirm the final RIDEM decision.
202947_11_ITEM8_P60_S0	In April 2009, the Company sued Power Test and Getty Properties Corp. in the Rhode Island Superior Court seeking remediation of the site or, in the alternative, the cost of the remediation.
202947_11_ITEM8_P60_S1	On May 1, 2009, Power Test and Getty Properties Corp. removed the action to the United States District Court for the District of Rhode Island.
202947_11_ITEM8_P61_S0	On May 22, 2009, Power Test and Getty Properties Corp. answered the Complaint and filed a Counterclaim against Dunellen, LLC and Capital Terminal Company alleging that Dunellen, LLC and Capital Terminal Company are responsible for the contamination.
202947_11_ITEM8_P61_S1	Getty Properties Corp. and Power Test have joined Getty Petroleum Marketing, Inc., the tenant under a long-term lease with Getty Properties Corp. of the adjacent property, as a defendant.
202947_11_ITEM8_P61_S2	The Company has amended its Complaint to add Getty Petroleum Marketing, Inc. as a defendant.
202947_11_ITEM8_P62_S0	In February 2011, the Company was notified by the United States District Court for the District of Rhode Island that the case was being transferred to the United States District Court for the District of New Hampshire due to a backlog of cases in Rhode Island.
202947_11_ITEM8_P63_S0	The parties are now engaged in discovery.
202947_11_ITEM8_P63_S1	There can be no assurance that the Company will prevail in this litigation.
202947_11_ITEM8_P64_S0	Since January 2003, the Company has not incurred significant costs in connection with this matter, other than ongoing litigation costs, and is unable to determine the costs it might incur to remedy the situation, as well as any costs to investigate, defend and seek reimbursement from the responsible party with respect to this contamination.
202947_11_ITEM8_P65_S0	In 1994, a leak was discovered in a 25,000 barrel storage tank at the Terminal which allowed the escape of a small amount of fuel oil.
202947_11_ITEM8_P65_S1	All required notices were made to RIDEM.
202947_11_ITEM8_P65_S2	In 2000, the tank was demolished and testing of the groundwater indicated that there was no large pooling of contaminants.
202947_11_ITEM8_P66_S0	In 2001, RIDEM approved a plan pursuant to which the Company installed a passive system consisting of three wells and commenced monitoring the wells.
202947_11_ITEM8_P67_S0	In 2003, RIDEM decided that the passive monitoring system previously approved was not sufficient and required the Company to design an active remediation system for the removal of product from the contaminated site.
202947_11_ITEM8_P67_S1	The Company and its consulting engineers began the pre-design testing of the site in the fourth quarter of 2004.
202947_11_ITEM8_P67_S2	The consulting engineers estimated a total cost of $200,000 to design, install and operate the system, which amount was accrued in 2004.
202947_11_ITEM8_P67_S3	Through 2006, the Company had expended $119,000 and has not incurred any additional costs since then.
202947_11_ITEM8_P67_S4	RIDEM has not taken any action on the Company s proposed plan.
202947_11_ITEM8_P68_S0	As designed, the system will pump out the contaminants which will be disposed of in compliance with applicable regulations.
202947_11_ITEM8_P68_S1	After a period of time, the groundwater will be tested to determine if sufficient contaminants have been removed.
202947_11_ITEM8_P68_S2	While the Company and its consulting engineers believe that the proposed active remediation system will correct the situation, it is possible that RIDEM could require the Company to expand remediation efforts, which could result in the Company incurring additional costs.
202947_11_ITEM8_P69_S0	The Pier is a deep-water pier in East Providence, Rhode Island owned by the Company which is integral to the operation of the Terminal.
202947_11_ITEM8_P69_S1	The Pier and the Terminal are connected by two petroleum pipelines which the Company has a permanent right to use.

202947_11_ITEM8_P84_S2	In order for the Company to qualify to be taxed as a REIT, the major shareholders ownership of the Company s issued and outstanding common stock would need to be reduced below the 50% level.

202947_12_ITEM7_P0_S0	Critical accounting policies: The Securities and Exchange Commission ( SEC ) has issued guidance for the disclosure of critical accounting policies.
202947_12_ITEM7_P0_S1	The SEC defines such policies as those that require application of management s most difficult, subjective or complex judgments, often as a result of the need to make estimates about the effect of matters that are inherently uncertain and may change in subsequent periods.
202947_12_ITEM7_P0_S2	The Company s significant accounting policies are described in Note 2 of Notes to Consolidated Financial Statements in Item 8.
202947_12_ITEM7_P0_S3	Not all of these significant accounting policies require management to make difficult, subjective or complex judgments or estimates.
202947_12_ITEM7_P0_S4	Management believes that the Company s revenue recognition policy for long-term leases with scheduled rent increases (leasing segment) meets the SEC definition of critical.
202947_12_ITEM7_P0_S5	Certain of the Company s long-term land leases have original terms of 30 to 149 years and contain scheduled rent increases where the future dollar increases are known at the time of the commencement of the lease or at a subsequent date.
202947_12_ITEM7_P0_S6	The first such lease commenced in 1988, had an original term of 99 years and provides for fixed percentage increases at specified intervals (as well as reappraisal increases).
202947_12_ITEM7_P0_S7	In accordance with United States generally accepted accounting principles in accounting for leases, rental income related to the fixed percentage increases that are presently known should be recognized on a straight-line basis.
202947_12_ITEM7_P0_S8	To calculate the annual straight-line amount, the 99 known annual rental amounts are totaled and this total is divided by 99.
202947_12_ITEM7_P0_S9	In 2009, a scheduled appraisal occurred, resulting in a rental increase.
202947_12_ITEM7_P0_S10	The Company recalculated the future annual straight-line amount using the remaining years under the lease.
202947_12_ITEM7_P0_S11	The turnaround date discussed below did not change.
202947_12_ITEM7_P1_S0	For this lease, the calculated annual straight-line amount for 1988 was eight times (multiple) the amount paid by the tenant under the terms of the lease (the contractual amount ).
202947_12_ITEM7_P1_S1	In subsequent years, as the tenant pays higher rents, the multiple gradually decreases until the 57 th year of the lease, at which time the contractual amount paid by the tenant will exceed the calculated straight-line amount.
202947_12_ITEM7_P1_S2	If the Company were to report annual revenue for this lease using the straight-line amount, it would record a significant receivable for each of the first 56 years, which receivable would grow to approximately $34,000,000.
202947_12_ITEM7_P1_S3	Management does not believe that the Company should record a receivable that would not begin to be collected until the 56 th year (the turnaround date ) since management could not be assured of collection.
202947_12_ITEM7_P1_S4	In 1988, management met with the SEC accounting staff to discuss its concerns in applying United States generally accepted accounting principles as they related to a lease of this length which results in the recording of such a significant receivable that would remain on the Company s balance sheet and continue to grow on an annual basis with a turnaround date so far in the future.
202947_12_ITEM7_P1_S5	The Company presented the SEC accounting staff with an application of the accounting policy whereby management would evaluate the collectability of the receivable on an annual basis and report as leasing revenue only that portion of the receivable that management could presently conclude would be collectible.
202947_12_ITEM7_P1_S6	The SEC accounting staff did not object to this application by the Company.
202947_12_ITEM7_P1_S7	Through December 31, 2011, the receivable on this lease has grown to $20,009,000 (cumulative excess of straight-line over contractual rentals) and management has not been able to conclude that any portion is collectible as the turnaround date is still 34 years away.
202947_12_ITEM7_P2_S0	In 2004, a second such lease commenced with an original term of 149 years and provides for fixed minimum percentage increases at specified intervals (as well as reappraisal increases).
202947_12_ITEM7_P2_S1	For this lease, the contractual amount paid by the tenant will not exceed the calculated straight-line amount until the 94 th year of the lease.
202947_12_ITEM7_P2_S2	Through December 31, 2011, the receivable on this lease is $18,197,000 (cumulative excess of straight-line over contractual rentals) and management has not been able to conclude that any portion is collectible as the turnaround date is 86 years away.
202947_12_ITEM7_P3_S0	In 2006, the Company entered into an Amended and Restated Agreement of its lease with Lamar Outdoor Advertising LLC ( Lamar ) with a current remaining term of 22 years which provides for fixed percentage increases annually.
202947_12_ITEM7_P3_S1	For this lease, the contractual amount paid by Lamar will not exceed the calculated straight-line amount until the 16 th year of the lease.
202947_12_ITEM7_P3_S2	Through December 31, 2011, the receivable on this lease is $1,205,000 (cumulative excess of straight-line over contractual rentals) and management has not been able to conclude that any portion is collectible as the turnaround date is 10 years away.
202947_12_ITEM7_P4_S0	Accordingly, the Company has not reported any portion of these amounts as leasing revenue in its consolidated financial statements and does not anticipate that it can reach such a conclusion until the turnaround dates are closer.
202947_12_ITEM7_P4_S1	Although the Company s other long-term land leases provide for scheduled rent increases, the provisions of the leases are such that certain future dollar amounts could not be calculated either at the time of the commencement of the lease or now, as such amounts are based on factors that are not presently known, i.e., future cost-of-living adjustments or future appraised values.
202947_12_ITEM7_P4_S2	Through December 31, 2011, the receivable on these leases is $10,109,000 and management has not been able to conclude that any portion is collectible as the turnaround dates are approximately 49 years away.

202947_12_ITEM8_P0_S1	We have audited the accompanying consolidated balance sheets of Capital Properties, Inc. and subsidiaries as of December 31, 2011 and 2010, and the related consolidated statements of income and retained earnings, and cash flows for the years then ended.
202947_12_ITEM8_P0_S2	These financial statements are the responsibility of the Company s management.
202947_12_ITEM8_P0_S3	Our responsibility is to express an opinion on these financial statements based on our audits.
202947_12_ITEM8_P0_S4	We conducted our audits in accordance with the standards of the Public Company Accounting Oversight Board (United States).
202947_12_ITEM8_P0_S5	Those standards require that we plan and perform the audit to obtain reasonable assurance about whether the financial statements are free of material misstatement.
202947_12_ITEM8_P0_S6	The Company is not required to have, nor were we engaged to perform, an audit of its internal control over financial reporting.
202947_12_ITEM8_P0_S7	An audit includes consideration of internal control over financial reporting as a basis for designing audit procedures that are appropriate in the circumstances, but not for the purpose of expressing an opinion on the effectiveness of the Company s internal control over financial reporting.
202947_12_ITEM8_P0_S8	Accordingly, we express no such opinion.
202947_12_ITEM8_P1_S0	An audit also includes examining, on a test basis, evidence supporting the amounts and disclosures in the financial statements, assessing the accounting principles used and significant estimates made by management and evaluating the overall financial statement presentation.
202947_12_ITEM8_P1_S1	We believe that our audits provide a reasonable basis for our opinion.
202947_12_ITEM8_P1_S2	In our opinion, the consolidated financial statements referred to above present fairly, in all material respects, the financial position of Capital Properties, Inc. and subsidiaries as of December 31, 2011 and 2010, and the results of their operations and their cash flows for the years then ended, in conformity with U.S. generally accepted accounting principles.

202947_12_ITEM8_P5_S0	Description of business: Capital Properties, Inc. and its wholly-owned subsidiaries, Tri-State Displays, Inc., Capital Terminal Company and Dunellen, LLC (collectively referred to as the Company ) operate in two segments, leasing and petroleum storage.
202947_12_ITEM8_P5_S1	The leasing segment consists of the long-term leasing of certain of its real estate interests in downtown Providence, Rhode Island (upon the commencement of which the tenants are required to construct buildings thereon, with the exception of a parking garage), the leasing of a portion of its building ( Steeple Street Building ) under short-term leasing arrangements and the leasing of locations along interstate and primary highways in Rhode Island and Massachusetts to Lamar Outdoor Advertising, LLC ( Lamar ) which has constructed outdoor advertising boards thereon.
202947_12_ITEM8_P5_S2	The Company anticipates that the future development of its remaining properties in and adjacent to the Capital Center area will consist primarily of long-term ground leases.
202947_12_ITEM8_P5_S3	Pending this development, the Company leases these parcels for public parking under short-term leasing arrangements to Metropark, Ltd. ( Metropark ).
202947_12_ITEM8_P6_S0	The petroleum storage segment consists of operating the petroleum storage terminal (the Terminal ) and the Wilkesbarre Pier (the Pier ), both of which are owned by the Company and are collectively referred to as the Facility, located in East Providence, Rhode Island, for Global Companies, LLC ( Global ) which stores and distributes petroleum products.
202947_12_ITEM8_P6_S1	The principal difference between the two segments relates to the nature of the operations.
202947_12_ITEM8_P7_S0	In the leasing segment, the tenants under long-term land leases incur substantially all of the development and operating costs of the assets constructed on the Company s land, including the payment of real property taxes on both the land and any improvements constructed thereon; whereas the Company is responsible for the operating and maintenance expenditures, including insurance and a portion of the real property taxes, as well as certain capital improvements at the Facility.
202947_12_ITEM8_P8_S0	Summary of significant accounting policies: Principles of consolidation: The accompanying consolidated financial statements include the accounts and transactions of the Company and its subsidiaries.
202947_12_ITEM8_P8_S1	All significant intercompany accounts and transactions have been eliminated in consolidation.
202947_12_ITEM8_P9_S0	Use of estimates: The preparation of consolidated financial statements in conformity with accounting principles generally accepted in the United States requires management to make estimates and assumptions that affect the reported amounts of assets and liabilities and disclosure of contingent assets and liabilities at the date of the financial statements.
202947_12_ITEM8_P9_S1	Estimates also affect the reported amounts of income and expenses during the reporting period.
202947_12_ITEM8_P9_S2	Actual results could differ from those estimates.
202947_12_ITEM8_P10_S0	Fair value of financial instruments: The Company believes that the fair values of its financial instruments, including cash, receivables and payables, approximate their respective book values because of their short-term nature.
202947_12_ITEM8_P10_S1	The fair value of the note payable approximates its book value and was determined using borrowing rates currently available to the Company for loans with similar terms and maturities.
202947_12_ITEM8_P11_S0	Properties and equipment: Properties and equipment are stated at cost.
202947_12_ITEM8_P11_S1	Acquisitions and additions are capitalized while routine maintenance and repairs, which do not improve the asset or extend its life, are charged to expense when incurred.
202947_12_ITEM8_P11_S2	Depreciation is being provided by the straight-line method over the estimated useful lives of the respective assets.
202947_12_ITEM8_P12_S0	The Company follows United States generally accepted accounting principles when accounting for the impairment or disposal of long-lived assets, which requires that properties and equipment held and used by the Company be reviewed for impairment whenever events or changes in circumstances indicate that the net book value of the asset may not be recoverable.
202947_12_ITEM8_P12_S1	An impairment loss will be recognized if the sum of the expected future cash flows (undiscounted and before interest) from the use of the asset is less than the net book value of the asset.
202947_12_ITEM8_P12_S2	Generally, the amount of the impairment loss is measured as the difference between the net book value and the estimated fair value of the asset.
202947_12_ITEM8_P13_S0	Cash and cash equivalents: The Company considers all highly liquid investments with a maturity of three months or less when purchased to be cash equivalents.
202947_12_ITEM8_P13_S1	At December 31, 2011 and 2010, the Company had no cash equivalents.
202947_12_ITEM8_P13_S2	The Company maintains all of its cash in non-interest bearing checking accounts in one bank which are fully insured by the Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation.
202947_12_ITEM8_P14_S0	Environmental incidents: The Company accrues a liability when an environmental incident has occurred and the costs are estimable.
202947_12_ITEM8_P14_S1	The Company does not record a receivable for recoveries from third parties for environmental matters until it has determined that the amount of the collection is reasonably assured.
202947_12_ITEM8_P14_S2	The accrued liability is relieved when the Company pays the liability or a third party assumes the liability.
202947_12_ITEM8_P14_S3	Upon determination that collection is reasonably assured or a third party assumes the liability, the Company records the amount as a reduction of expense.
202947_12_ITEM8_P15_S0	The Company charges to expense those costs that do not extend the life, increase the capacity or improve the safety or efficiency of the property owned or used by the Company.
202947_12_ITEM8_P16_S0	Revenues: Leasing The Company s properties leased to others are under operating leases.
202947_12_ITEM8_P16_S1	The Company reports leasing revenue when earned under the operating method.
202947_12_ITEM8_P16_S2	Certain of the Company s long-term land leases, including the outdoor advertising locations, provide for presently known scheduled rent increases over the remaining terms (22 to 143 years).
202947_12_ITEM8_P16_S3	The Company follows United States generally accepted accounting principles in accounting for leases by recognizing leasing revenue on the straight-line basis over the terms of the leases; however, the Company does not report as revenue that portion of such straight-line rentals which management is unable to conclude is realizable (collectible) due to the length of the lease terms and other related uncertainties.
202947_12_ITEM8_P17_S0	Petroleum storage facility The Company reports revenue from the operations of the Facility when earned and reports as revenue the tenant s portion of the real property taxes and certain other items as required by the lease.
202947_12_ITEM8_P17_S1	Contingent The Company reports contingent revenue in the period in which the factors occur on which the contingent payments are predicated.
202947_12_ITEM8_P18_S0	Income taxes: The Company and its subsidiaries file consolidated income tax returns.
202947_12_ITEM8_P18_S1	The Company provides for income taxes based on income reported for financial reporting purposes.
202947_12_ITEM8_P18_S2	The provision for income taxes differs from the amounts currently payable because of temporary differences associated with the recognition of certain income and expense items for financial reporting and tax reporting purposes.
202947_12_ITEM8_P18_S3	The Company follows United States generally accepted accounting principles in accounting for uncertainty in income taxes.

202947_12_ITEM8_P18_S5	The Company will report any tax-related interest and penalties related to uncertain tax positions as a component of income tax expense.

202947_12_ITEM8_P36_S0	On August 31, 2011, while excavating in connection with the construction of a highway for the Rhode Island Department of Transportation ( RIDOT ), Cardi Corporation ( Cardi ) ruptured an underground pipeline controlled and used by the Company for the transportation of Ultra Low Sulfur Diesel ( ULSD ) from the Wilkesbarre Pier to its Petroleum Storage Facility.
202947_12_ITEM8_P36_S1	At the time, the Company was receiving product from a barge and, as a result of the rupture, approximately 70,000 gallons of ULSD were discharged.
202947_12_ITEM8_P37_S0	Pursuant to the Company s Emergency Response Plan, representatives of the Company took control of the spill site and coordinated the response of various governmental agencies as well as private contractors.
202947_12_ITEM8_P37_S1	Approximately 56,000 gallons of spilled diesel were recovered.
202947_12_ITEM8_P37_S2	On September 6, 2011, the Company turned over the responsibility for the clean-up to Cardi.
202947_12_ITEM8_P37_S3	The Company notified the required government agencies and its insurance carriers of the rupture.
202947_12_ITEM8_P37_S4	Management s estimate of the total cost incurred by the Company in responding to the emergency and repairing the pipeline was $349,000, which amount was accrued as an expense at September 30, 2011, and the Company determined that no receivable could be recorded at that time.
202947_12_ITEM8_P38_S0	which amount was offset against the expense previously recorded.
202947_12_ITEM8_P38_S1	At December 31, 2011, the Company determined that $184,000 of the remaining liability was assumed by Cardi.
202947_12_ITEM8_P38_S2	The Company reduced the previously recorded liability and expense by that amount.
202947_12_ITEM8_P38_S3	In February 2012, Cardi paid the $184,000.
202947_12_ITEM8_P38_S4	The Company has determined that no receivable can be recorded at this time for the remaining $76,000.
202947_12_ITEM8_P38_S5	During the fourth quarter of 2011, the Company paid an additional $14,000 in connection with the pipeline rupture for which the Company has not yet received payment and for which no receivable has been recorded.
202947_12_ITEM8_P38_S6	The $90,000 is presented as a separate line item within petroleum storage facility expenses on the accompanying consolidated statement of income and retained earnings for the year ended December 31, 2011.
202947_12_ITEM8_P38_S7	The Company believes that it has no liability with respect to the discharge and has asserted a claim against Cardi and RIDOT for the costs and other damages incurred by the Company.
202947_12_ITEM8_P39_S0	ULSD incident (2011): In March 2011, management learned that, during the normal receipt of product from a barge, No. 2 heating oil (high sulfur heating oil) was accidentally pumped into one of the Company s ULSD petroleum storage tanks (Tank 67), resulting in a mixture with a sulfur content in excess of that allowed by the Environmental Protection Agency ( EPA ).
202947_12_ITEM8_P39_S1	The Company notified Global and its insurance carriers of the incident.
202947_12_ITEM8_P39_S2	Global informed the Company that it had contacted its customers that received the mixture and commenced a sampling and testing program with certain of its customers to determine (1) if any product should be removed and replaced with conforming product or (2) if the product need only be treated to meet the EPA requirements.
202947_12_ITEM8_P40_S0	In August 2011, Global asserted a claim against the Company of $132,000 for damages incurred by Global arising out of the incident, which amount was accrued as an expense at September 30, 2011.
202947_12_ITEM8_P40_S1	At December 31, 2011, the Company determined that its insurance carrier had assumed this liability, and the Company reduced the previously recorded liability and expense by that amount.
202947_12_ITEM8_P40_S2	In March 2012, the Company s insurance carrier paid Global the full amount of its claim, and Global released the Company of all liability relating to this incident.
202947_12_ITEM8_P41_S0	Tank 153 (2010): On August 30, 2010, during a regular facility inspection of the Terminal, a release of petroleum-contaminated water was discovered from the tank bottom of one of the Company s 150,000 barrel tanks (Tank 153).
202947_12_ITEM8_P41_S1	The Company notified the Rhode Island Department of Environmental Management ( RIDEM ), the EPA and the United States Coast Guard.
202947_12_ITEM8_P41_S2	It also notified its insurance carriers of the release and the damage to the tank.
202947_12_ITEM8_P41_S3	The tank was emptied of product and the cleaning of the tank bottom was completed in September 2010.
202947_12_ITEM8_P41_S4	The petroleum-contaminated water released from the tank was contained on the secondary containment liner under the tank bottom, preventing contamination of the groundwater.
202947_12_ITEM8_P41_S5	The Company engaged an outside engineering firm to inspect the tank bottom to determine the cause and location of the release, as well as the extent of the required repairs.
202947_12_ITEM8_P41_S6	The findings of the inspection indicated that aggressive corrosion from inside the tank occurred, causing two holes in the immediate vicinity of the observed release, as well as several other holes or potential holes in other areas of the tank bottom.
202947_12_ITEM8_P41_S7	The report concluded that the corrosion was caused by microbial contamination, which was affirmed by a corrosion specialist.
202947_12_ITEM8_P41_S8	The final cost of the cleanup, inspection and repair of the tank was $533,000, all of which was recorded as an expense at December 31, 2010.
202947_12_ITEM8_P41_S9	The tank was placed back in service in February 2011.
202947_12_ITEM8_P41_S10	In June 2011, Global paid the Company $458,000 which is recorded in petroleum storage facility revenues, reimbursement of tank repairs on the accompanying consolidated statement of income and retained earnings for the year ended December 31, 2011 due to the contractual nature of the reimbursement.
202947_12_ITEM8_P41_S11	The difference relates to the $75,000 cost of epoxy coating the bottom of Tank 153 which the Company paid.
202947_12_ITEM8_P42_S0	The testing of certain of the Company s other tanks revealed the presence of corrosive microbial contaminants in Tanks 151 and 32.
202947_12_ITEM8_P42_S1	Both tanks were treated with a biocide and continue to be monitored and treated as necessary.
202947_12_ITEM8_P42_S2	Since Tank 32 had been inspected in June 2010, the Company believes that the contaminants have not affected the integrity of this tank bottom.
202947_12_ITEM8_P42_S3	However, since Tank 151 had not been inspected since construction in 2006, the Company took this tank out of service in February 2011.
202947_12_ITEM8_P42_S4	The tank was emptied of product, and an inspection of the tank bottom revealed minor corrosion.
202947_12_ITEM8_P42_S5	The Company completed the repairs recommended by the inspectors and applied an epoxy coating to the bottom of Tank 151 at a cost of $50,000, which has been included in petroleum storage facility expenses, operating on the accompanying consolidated statement of income and retained earnings for the year ended December 31, 2011.
202947_12_ITEM8_P42_S6	The tank was back in service in May 2011.
202947_12_ITEM8_P42_S7	Exclusive of the epoxy coating, the total cost of cleanup, inspection and repair of the tanks was $40,000 which Global paid the Company in September 2011 and is recorded in petroleum storage facilities revenues, reimbursement of tank repairs on the accompanying consolidated statement of income and retained earnings for the year ended December 31, 2011.
202947_12_ITEM8_P42_S8	Tank repairs related to this incident have been presented as a separate line item within petroleum storage facility expenses on the accompanying consolidated statement of income and retained earnings.
202947_12_ITEM8_P42_S9	Routine tank repairs continue to be included with petroleum storage facility operating expenses on the accompanying consolidated statements of income and retained earnings.
202947_12_ITEM8_P43_S0	Environmental incident (2002): In 2002, during testing of monitoring wells at the Terminal, the Company s consulting engineer discovered free floating phase product in a groundwater monitoring well located on that portion of the Terminal purchased in 2000.
202947_12_ITEM8_P43_S1	Laboratory analysis indicated that the product was gasoline, which is not a product the Company ever stored at the Terminal.
202947_12_ITEM8_P43_S2	The Company commenced an environmental investigation and analysis, the results of which indicate that the gasoline did not come from the Terminal.
202947_12_ITEM8_P43_S3	RIDEM subsequently identified Power Test Realty Partnership ( Power Test ), the owner of an adjacent parcel, as a potentially responsible party for the contamination.
202947_12_ITEM8_P43_S4	Getty Properties Corp. is the general partner of Power Test.
202947_12_ITEM8_P44_S0	Power Test challenged that determination and, after an administrative hearing, in October 2008 a RIDEM Hearing Officer determined that Power Test is responsible for the discharge of the petroleum product under the Rhode Island Oil Pollution Control Act, R.I.G.L. Section 46-12.5.1-3 and Rule 6(a) and 12(b) of the Oil Pollution Control Regulations.
202947_12_ITEM8_P44_S1	The RIDEM Decision and Order requires Power Test to remediate the contamination as directed by RIDEM and remanded the proposed penalty to RIDEM for recalculation.
202947_12_ITEM8_P44_S2	In November 2008, Power Test appealed the decision to the Rhode Island Superior Court.
202947_12_ITEM8_P44_S3	In addition, in November 2008, Power Test sought, and received, a stay of the Decision and Order of the Hearing Officer pending a clarification by RIDEM of the amount of the proposed penalty.
202947_12_ITEM8_P44_S4	In October 2009, RIDEM issued a recalculated administrative penalty, and, subsequently, the RIDEM Hearing Officer issued a recommended amended decision, which was affirmed as a final decision by the RIDEM Director in December 2009.
202947_12_ITEM8_P44_S5	In January 2010, Power Test appealed that decision to Superior Court.
202947_12_ITEM8_P44_S6	In September 2011, the Superior Court affirmed the decision of the RIDEM director.
202947_12_ITEM8_P44_S7	Power Test has appealed that decision to the Rhode Island Supreme Court.
202947_12_ITEM8_P45_S0	In April 2009, the Company sued Power Test and Getty Properties Corp. in the Rhode Island Superior Court seeking remediation of the site or, in the alternative, the cost of the remediation.
202947_12_ITEM8_P45_S1	On May 1, 2009, Power Test and Getty Properties Corp. removed the action to the United States District Court for the District of Rhode Island.
202947_12_ITEM8_P46_S0	On May 22, 2009, Power Test and Getty Properties Corp. answered the Complaint and filed a Counterclaim against Dunellen, LLC and Capital Terminal Company alleging that Dunellen, LLC and Capital Terminal Company are responsible for the contamination.
202947_12_ITEM8_P46_S1	Getty Properties Corp. and Power Test have joined Getty Petroleum Marketing, Inc., the tenant under a long-term lease with Getty Properties Corp. of the adjacent property, as a defendant.
202947_12_ITEM8_P46_S2	The Company has amended its Complaint to add Getty Petroleum Marketing, Inc. as a defendant.
202947_12_ITEM8_P47_S0	On December 5, 2011, Getty Petroleum Marketing, Inc., filed for bankruptcy under Chapter 11 of the United States Bankruptcy Act.
202947_12_ITEM8_P47_S1	The parties are now engaged in discovery.
202947_12_ITEM8_P47_S2	There can be no assurance that the Company will prevail in this litigation.
202947_12_ITEM8_P47_S3	Since January 2003, the Company has not incurred significant costs in connection with this matter, other than ongoing litigation costs, and is unable to determine the costs it might incur to remedy the situation, as well as any costs to investigate, defend and seek reimbursement from the responsible party with respect to this contamination.
202947_12_ITEM8_P48_S0	In 1994, a leak was discovered in a 25,000 barrel storage tank at the Terminal which allowed the escape of a small amount of fuel oil.
202947_12_ITEM8_P48_S1	All required notices were made to RIDEM.
202947_12_ITEM8_P48_S2	In 2000, the tank was demolished and testing of the groundwater indicated that there was no large pooling of contaminants.
202947_12_ITEM8_P49_S0	In 2001, RIDEM approved a plan pursuant to which the Company installed a passive system consisting of three wells and commenced monitoring the wells.
202947_12_ITEM8_P49_S1	In 2003, RIDEM decided that the passive monitoring system previously approved was not sufficient and required the Company to design an active remediation system for the removal of product from the contaminated site.
202947_12_ITEM8_P49_S2	The Company and its consulting engineers began the pre-design testing of the site in the fourth quarter of 2004.
202947_12_ITEM8_P49_S3	The consulting engineers estimated a total cost of $200,000 to design, install and operate the system, which amount was accrued in 2004.
202947_12_ITEM8_P49_S4	Through 2006, the Company had expended $119,000 and has not incurred any additional costs since then.
202947_12_ITEM8_P49_S5	In 2011, RIDEM notified the company to proceed with the next phase of the approval process, notifying the abutters of the proposed remediation system even though RIDEM has not yet taken any action on the Company s proposed plan.
202947_12_ITEM8_P50_S0	As designed, the system will pump out the contaminants which will be disposed of in compliance with applicable regulations.
202947_12_ITEM8_P50_S1	After a period of time, the groundwater will be tested to determine if sufficient contaminants have been removed.
202947_12_ITEM8_P50_S2	While the Company and its consulting engineers believe that the proposed active remediation system will correct the situation, it is possible that RIDEM could require the Company to expand remediation efforts, which could result in the Company incurring costs in excess of the remaining accrual of $81,000.

202947_12_ITEM8_P55_S0	In November 2008, the Company restated its Articles of Incorporation:
202947_12_ITEM8_P56_S0	To provide for certain transfer and ownership restrictions as set forth therein.
202947_12_ITEM8_P57_S0	In December 2008, the Company issued (in the form of a stock dividend) 3,299,956 shares of Class B Common Stock on a one-for-one basis for each share of Class A Common Stock held.
202947_12_ITEM8_P57_S1	The holders of Class A and Class B Common Stock vote together as a single class on all matters submitted to the shareholders of the Company except for the election of the Board of Directors and except in connection with certain major corporate actions, including a sale of the Company.
202947_12_ITEM8_P57_S2	The holders of Class A Common Stock, voting as a separate class, elect one-third of the Board of Directors.
202947_12_ITEM8_P57_S3	The holders of Class B Common Stock, voting as a separate class, elect the remainder of the Board of Directors.
202947_12_ITEM8_P58_S0	Class B Common Stock is convertible by the record owner thereof into the same number of shares of Class A Common Stock at any time.
202947_12_ITEM8_P58_S1	For the years ended December 31, 2011 and 2010, the number of shares converted were 16,318 shares and 74,860 shares, respectively.
202947_12_ITEM8_P59_S0	The Class A Common Stock is listed on the Premier QX Tier of the OTCQX.
202947_12_ITEM8_P59_S1	The Class B Common Stock is not listed on any national or regional stock exchange, or on the National Association of Securities Dealers Automated Quotation National Market System or on the OTCQX.
202947_12_ITEM8_P60_S0	The holders of Class A and Class B Common Stock share equally in the earnings of the Company and in dividends declared by the Company.
202947_12_ITEM8_P60_S1	The Company s Restated Articles of Incorporation prohibits any shareholder from acquiring more than a 5% interest in the Company s classes of common stock and prohibits any shareholder or any beneficial owner who, at the time of the filing of the Restated Articles of Incorporation owned 5% or more of the Company s classes of common stock from increasing their aggregate percentage ownership of both classes of common stock.
202947_12_ITEM8_P60_S2	Should a shareholder acquire a number of shares that results in the limitation being exceeded, shares in excess of the limitation would be automatically converted into an equal number of shares of Excess Stock, which class was authorized pursuant to the 2001 Amendment to the Company s Articles of Incorporation.
202947_12_ITEM8_P60_S3	Excess Stock is non-voting and is not entitled to dividends.
202947_12_ITEM8_P60_S4	However, the shareholder may designate a qualifying transferee for shares of Excess Stock, at which time such shares would be converted and reissued as Class A or Class B Common shares as the case may be.
202947_12_ITEM8_P61_S0	The purpose for creating the Class B Common Stock was to put the Company in the position to qualify to be taxed as a real estate investment trust ( REIT ).
202947_12_ITEM8_P61_S1	One of the qualifications to be taxed as a REIT is that no more than 50% of the shares of a company can be held by five or fewer individuals during the last half of each taxable year.
202947_12_ITEM8_P61_S2	Currently, the majority shareholder controls 52.3% of the Company s outstanding common stock and three other shareholders each own more than 5% of the Company s outstanding common stock.
202947_12_ITEM8_P61_S3	In order for the Company to qualify to be taxed as a REIT, the major shareholders ownership of the Company s issued and outstanding common stock would need to be reduced below the 50% level.

202947_12_ITEM8_P65_S0	Related party transaction: The Company and Providence and Worcester Railroad Company ( the Railroad ) have a common controlling shareholder.
202947_12_ITEM8_P66_S0	The Company has the right to use certain pipelines located in the right of way of the Railroad which were constructed by Getty Oil Company (Eastern Operations), Inc. ( GettyEO ).
202947_12_ITEM8_P66_S1	Pursuant to an agreement between the Railroad and GettyEO dated August 6, 1975, the Railroad has the right to relocate any portion of the pipelines located within the Railroad s right of way.
202947_12_ITEM8_P66_S2	The Company has supported an extension of Waterfront Drive, so-called, up to Dexter Road and adjacent to the Company s Terminal, which road is being constructed on the Railroad right of way.
202947_12_ITEM8_P66_S3	The State of Rhode Island s plans for the Waterfront Drive extension required a relocation of a portion of the pipelines which the Railroad has the right to relocate.
202947_12_ITEM8_P66_S4	RIDOT entered into an agreement with the Railroad (the RIDOT Agreement ) to reimburse the Railroad for reasonable costs incurred by it in relocating the pipelines, which were originally estimated to be $159,000.
202947_12_ITEM8_P66_S5	Any substantial change to the estimate requires the approval of RIDOT.
202947_12_ITEM8_P67_S0	In May 2011, the Company entered into an agreement with the Railroad to act as the Railroad s agent with respect to the relocation of the pipelines.
202947_12_ITEM8_P67_S1	The Company, without receiving compensation, is obligated under the agreement to select, direct and supervise all subcontractors subject to the Railroad s approval.
202947_12_ITEM8_P68_S0	Upon the Railroad s receipt of invoices from the contractors, the Railroad requires the Company to verify the accuracy of the invoices and submit a check to the Railroad covering the amount of the invoices.
202947_12_ITEM8_P68_S1	The Railroad pays the invoices, using the funds advanced by the Company.
202947_12_ITEM8_P68_S2	The Railroad is then obligated to submit the invoices to RIDOT for reimbursement.
202947_12_ITEM8_P68_S3	Any reimbursements received from RIDOT are required to be paid to the Company in a timely manner.
202947_12_ITEM8_P68_S4	Any shortfall in RIDOT s reimbursement is borne by the Company.
202947_12_ITEM8_P68_S5	At December 31, 2011, costs incurred to relocate the pipeline totaled $219,000, which amount is included in prepaid and other on the accompanying consolidated balance sheet at December 31, 2011.
202947_12_ITEM8_P68_S6	Of this amount, the Company had made a cash advance of $119,000 to the Railroad by December 31, 2011.
202947_12_ITEM8_P68_S7	The Railroad submitted the total amount to RIDOT in February 2012 and has not yet received any reimbursements.
202947_12_ITEM8_P68_S8	The Railroad and the Company have discussed with RIDOT the $60,000 in excess costs incurred to complete the project but no acceptance by RIDOT has yet been made.
202947_12_ITEM8_P68_S9	The Company believes, based on its discussions with RIDOT, that reimbursement to the Railroad and ultimately the Company, is reasonably assured.

202947_12_ITEM9_P0_S0	financial disclosure as defined by Item 304 of Regulation S-K. Item 9A. Controls and Procedures Under the supervision of the Company s management, including its principal executive officer and principal financial officer, the Company has evaluated the effectiveness of the design and operation of its disclosure controls and procedures (as defined in Rule 13a-15 under the Securities Exchange Act of 1934) as of the end of the period covered by this report.
202947_12_ITEM9_P0_S1	Based upon this evaluation, the principal executive officer and principal financial officer have concluded that, as of such date, the Company s disclosure controls and procedures were effective in making them aware on a timely basis of the material information relating to the Company required to be included in the Company s periodic filings with the Securities and Exchange Commission.
202947_12_ITEM9_P1_S0	The Company s management is responsible for establishing and maintaining adequate internal control over financial reporting (as such term is defined in Rules 13a-15(f) and 15d-15(f) under the Exchange Act).
202947_12_ITEM9_P1_S1	The Company s internal control over financial reporting is designed to provide reasonable assurance regarding the reliability of its financial reporting and the preparation of published financial statements in accordance with generally accepted accounting principles.
202947_12_ITEM9_P1_S2	However, because of its inherent limitations, internal control over financial reporting may not prevent or detect misstatements.
202947_12_ITEM9_P1_S3	Therefore, even those systems determined to be effective can provide only reasonable assurance with respect to financial statement preparation and presentation.
202947_12_ITEM9_P1_S4	Also, projections of any evaluation of effectiveness to future periods are subject to the risk that controls may become inadequate because of changes in conditions, or the degree of compliance with policies may deteriorate.
202947_12_ITEM9_P2_S0	Management conducted its evaluation of the effectiveness of its internal control over financial reporting based on the framework in Internal Control-Integrated Framework issued by the Committee of Sponsoring Organizations of the Treadway Commission ( COSO ) as of December 31, 2011.
202947_12_ITEM9_P2_S1	Based on this assessment, the principal executive officer and principal financial officer believe that as of December 31, 2011, the Company s internal control over financial reporting was effective based on criteria set forth by COSO in Internal Control-Integrated Framework.
202947_12_ITEM9_P2_S2	This annual report does not include an attestation report of the Company s independent registered public accounting firm regarding internal control over financial reporting.
202947_12_ITEM9_P2_S3	Management s report was not subject to attestation by the Company s independent registered public accounting firm pursuant to rules of the Securities and Exchange Commission that permit the Company to provide only management s report in this annual report.
