202947_12_ITEM12_P1_S0	Certain Relationships and Related Transactions and Director Independence The Company and Providence Worcester Railroad Company ( the Railroad ) have a common controlling shareholder.
202947_12_ITEM12_P2_S0	The Company has the right to use certain pipelines located in the Railroad s right of way which were constructed by Getty Oil Company (Eastern Operations), Inc. ( GettyEO ).
202947_12_ITEM12_P2_S1	Pursuant to an agreement between the Railroad and GettyEO dated August 6, 1975, the Railroad has the right to relocate any portion of the pipelines located within the Railroad s right of way.
202947_12_ITEM12_P2_S2	The Company has supported an extension of Waterfront Drive, so-called, up to Dexter Road and adjacent to the Company s Terminal, which road is being constructed on the Railroad right of way.
202947_12_ITEM12_P2_S3	The State of Rhode Island s plans for the Waterfront Drive extension required a relocation of a portion of the pipelines which the Railroad has the right to relocate.
202947_12_ITEM12_P2_S4	RIDOT entered into an agreement with the Railroad (the RIDOT Agreement ) to reimburse the Railroad for reasonable costs incurred by it in relocating the pipelines, which were originally estimated to be $159,000.
202947_12_ITEM12_P2_S5	Any substantial change to the estimate requires the approval of RIDOT.
202947_12_ITEM12_P3_S0	In May 2011, the Company entered into an agreement with the Railroad to act as the Railroad s agent with respect to the relocation of the pipelines.
202947_12_ITEM12_P3_S1	The Company, without receiving compensation, is obligated under the agreement to select, direct and supervise all subcontractors subject to the Railroad s approval.
202947_12_ITEM12_P4_S0	Upon the Railroad s receipt of invoices from the contractors, the Railroad requires the Company to verify the accuracy of the invoices and submit a check to the Railroad covering the amount of the invoices.
202947_12_ITEM12_P4_S1	The Railroad pays the invoices, using the funds advanced by the Company.
202947_12_ITEM12_P4_S2	The Railroad is then obligated to submit the invoices to RIDOT for reimbursement.
202947_12_ITEM12_P4_S3	Any reimbursements received from RIDOT are required to be paid to the Company in a timely manner.
202947_12_ITEM12_P4_S4	Any shortfall in RIDOT s reimbursement is borne by the Company.
202947_12_ITEM12_P5_S0	At December 31, 2011, costs incurred to relocate the pipeline totaled $219,000.
202947_12_ITEM12_P5_S1	Of this amount, the Company had made a cash advance of $119,000 to the Railroad by December 31, 2011.
202947_12_ITEM12_P5_S2	The Railroad submitted the total amount to RIDOT in February 2012 and has not yet received any reimbursements.
202947_12_ITEM12_P5_S3	The Railroad and the Company have discussed with RIDOT the $60,000 in excess costs incurred to complete the project but no acceptance by RIDOT has yet been made.
202947_12_ITEM12_P5_S4	The Company believes, based on its discussions with RIDOT, that reimbursement to the Railroad and ultimately the Company, is reasonably assured.

202947_13_ITEM7_P0_S0	Critical accounting policies: The Securities and Exchange Commission ( SEC ) has issued guidance for the disclosure of critical accounting policies.
202947_13_ITEM7_P0_S1	The SEC defines such policies as those that require application of management s most difficult, subjective or complex judgments, often as a result of the need to make estimates about the effect of matters that are inherently uncertain and may change in subsequent periods.
202947_13_ITEM7_P0_S2	The Company s significant accounting policies are described in Note 2 of Notes to Consolidated Financial Statements in Item 8.
202947_13_ITEM7_P0_S3	Not all of these significant accounting policies require management to make difficult, subjective or complex judgments or estimates.
202947_13_ITEM7_P0_S4	Management believes that the Company s revenue recognition policy for long-term leases with scheduled rent increases (leasing segment) meets the SEC definition of critical.
202947_13_ITEM7_P0_S5	Certain of the Company s long-term land leases have original terms of 30 to 149 years and contain scheduled rent increases where the future dollar increases are known at the time of the commencement of the lease or at a subsequent date.
202947_13_ITEM7_P0_S6	The first such lease commenced in 1988, had an original term of 99 years and provides for fixed percentage increases at specified intervals (as well as reappraisal increases).
202947_13_ITEM7_P1_S0	In accordance with United States generally accepted accounting principles ( GAAP ) in accounting for leases, rental income related to the fixed percentage increases that are presently known should be recognized on a straight-line basis.
202947_13_ITEM7_P1_S1	To calculate the annual straight-line amount, the 99 known annual rental amounts are totaled and this total is divided by 99.
202947_13_ITEM7_P1_S2	In 2009, a scheduled appraisal occurred, resulting in a rental increase.
202947_13_ITEM7_P1_S3	The Company recalculated the future annual straight-line amount using the remaining years under the lease.
202947_13_ITEM7_P1_S4	The turnaround date discussed below did not change.
202947_13_ITEM7_P2_S0	For this lease, the calculated annual straight-line amount for 1988 was eight times (multiple) the amount paid by the tenant under the terms of the lease (the contractual amount ).
202947_13_ITEM7_P2_S1	In subsequent years, as the tenant pays higher rents, the multiple gradually decreases until the 57 th year of the lease, at which time the contractual amount paid by the tenant will exceed the calculated straight-line amount.
202947_13_ITEM7_P2_S2	If the Company were to report annual revenue for this lease using the straight-line amount, it would record a significant receivable for each of the first 56 years, which receivable would grow to approximately $34,000,000.
202947_13_ITEM7_P2_S3	Management does not believe that the Company should record a receivable that would not begin to be collected until the 56 th year (the turnaround date ) since management could not be assured of collection.
202947_13_ITEM7_P2_S4	In 1988, management met with the SEC accounting staff to discuss its concerns in applying GAAP as it related to a lease of this length which results in the recording of such a significant receivable that would remain on the Company s balance sheet and continue to grow on an annual basis with a turnaround date so far in the future.
202947_13_ITEM7_P2_S5	The Company presented the SEC accounting staff with an application of the accounting policy whereby management would evaluate the collectability of the receivable on an annual basis and report as leasing revenue only that portion of the receivable that management could presently conclude would be collectible.
202947_13_ITEM7_P2_S6	The SEC accounting staff did not object to this application by the Company.
202947_13_ITEM7_P2_S7	Through December 31, 2012, the receivable on this lease has grown to $20,728,000 (cumulative excess of straight-line over contractual rentals) and management has not been able to conclude that any portion is collectible as the turnaround date is still 33 years away.
202947_13_ITEM7_P3_S0	In 2004, a second such lease commenced with an original term of 149 years and provides for fixed minimum percentage increases at specified intervals (as well as reappraisal increases).
202947_13_ITEM7_P3_S1	For this lease, the contractual amount paid by the tenant will not exceed the calculated straight-line amount until the 94 th year of the lease.
202947_13_ITEM7_P3_S2	Through December 31, 2012, the receivable on this lease is $20,310,000 (cumulative excess of straight-line over contractual rentals) and management has not been able to conclude that any portion is collectible as the turnaround date is 85 years away.
202947_13_ITEM7_P4_S0	In 2006, the Company entered into an Amended and Restated Agreement of its lease with Lamar Outdoor Advertising LLC ( Lamar ) with a current remaining term of 21 years which provides for fixed percentage increases annually.
202947_13_ITEM7_P4_S1	For this lease, the contractual amount paid by Lamar will not exceed the calculated straight-line amount until the 16 th year of the lease.
202947_13_ITEM7_P4_S2	Through December 31, 2012, the receivable on this lease is $1,368,000 (cumulative excess of straight-line over contractual rentals) and management has not been able to conclude that any portion is collectible as the turnaround date is nine years away.
202947_13_ITEM7_P5_S0	Accordingly, the Company has not reported any portion of these amounts as leasing revenue in its consolidated financial statements and does not anticipate that it can reach such a conclusion until the turnaround dates are closer.
202947_13_ITEM7_P5_S1	Although the Company s other long-term land leases provide for scheduled rent increases, the provisions of the leases are such that certain future dollar amounts could not be calculated either at the time of the commencement of the lease or now, as such amounts are based on factors that are not presently known, i.e., future cost-of-living adjustments or future appraised values.
202947_13_ITEM7_P5_S2	Through December 31, 2012, the receivable on these leases is $11,239,000 and management has not been able to conclude that any portion is collectible as the turnaround dates are approximately 48 years away.
202947_13_ITEM7_P6_S0	Segments: The Company operates in two segments: leasing and petroleum storage.
202947_13_ITEM7_P6_S1	The leasing segment consists of the long-term leasing of certain of its real estate interests in downtown Providence, Rhode Island (upon the commencement of which the tenants have been required to construct buildings thereon, with the exception of the parking garage and Parcels 6B and 6C), the leasing of a portion of the Steeple Street Building under short-term leasing arrangements and the leasing of locations along interstate and primary highways in Rhode Island and Massachusetts to Lamar which has constructed outdoor advertising boards thereon.
202947_13_ITEM7_P6_S2	The Company anticipates that the future development of its remaining properties in and adjacent to the Capital Center area will consist primarily of long-term ground leases.
202947_13_ITEM7_P6_S3	Pending this development, the Company leases these parcels for public parking under short-term leasing arrangements to Metropark.
202947_13_ITEM7_P7_S0	The petroleum storage segment consists of operating the Facility in East Providence, Rhode Island, for Global Companies, LLC ( Global ).
202947_13_ITEM7_P7_S1	The principal difference between the two segments relates to the nature of the operations.
202947_13_ITEM7_P8_S0	In the leasing segment, the tenants under the long-term land leases incur substantially all of the development and operating costs of the assets constructed on the Company s land, including the payment of real property taxes on both the land and any improvements constructed thereon; whereas the Company is responsible for the operating and maintenance expenditures, including insurance and a portion of the real property taxes, as well as certain capital improvements at the Facility.
202947_13_ITEM7_P9_S0	Results of operations: Year Ended December 31, 2012 Compared to Year Ended December 31, 2011 Leasing segment: Leasing revenues increased due to scheduled increases in rentals under long-term land leases.
202947_13_ITEM7_P9_S1	Leasing expense remained at the 2011 level.
202947_13_ITEM7_P10_S0	In June 2011, Global reimbursed the Company $458,000 for certain costs associated with the cleanup, inspection and repair of a tank (which costs were recorded in 2010) and an additional $53,000 for tank repairs.
202947_13_ITEM7_P10_S1	Exclusive of these amounts, petroleum storage facility revenues increased $104,000 due to scheduled annual cost-of-living adjustments under the lease for the petroleum storage facility.
202947_13_ITEM7_P11_S0	In connection with a pipeline breach in August 2011 by Cardi Corporation ( Cardi ), at September 30, 2011, management estimated that the total cost incurred by the Company in responding to the emergency and repairing the pipeline was $349,000, which amount was accrued as an expense.
202947_13_ITEM7_P11_S1	In November 2011, Cardi paid the Company $89,000, which amount was offset against the expense previously recorded.
202947_13_ITEM7_P11_S2	During the fourth quarter of 2011, the Company paid an additional $14,000 in connection with the pipeline rupture.
202947_13_ITEM7_P11_S3	At December 31, 2011, the Company determined that $184,000 of the remaining liability was assumed by Cardi.
202947_13_ITEM7_P12_S0	recorded liability and expense by that amount.
202947_13_ITEM7_P12_S1	In February 2012, Cardi paid the $184,000.
202947_13_ITEM7_P12_S2	In May 2012, Cardi paid both the remaining $76,000 and the $14,000, and the Company reduced the accrued liability and recorded the $90,000 as a reduction of expense.
202947_13_ITEM7_P12_S3	Exclusive of the $90,000, petroleum storage facility expense remained approximately at the 2011 level.

202947_13_ITEM7_P14_S2	The existing note to the Bank was amended and now bears interest at an annual rate of 3.34% for the first five years and thereafter will bear interest on either a floating rate basis at LIBOR plus 215 basis points with a floor of 3.25% or a fixed rate of 225 basis points over the five-year Federal Home Loan Bank of Boston Classic Advance Rate.
202947_13_ITEM7_P14_S3	The loan has a term of ten years with repayments on a 20-year amortization schedule (monthly payments of $24,000 plus interest) and a balloon payment of $2,869,000 in December 2022 when the loan matures.

202947_13_ITEM7_P15_S5	Net Proceeds means the gross cash received by the Company from any such sale reduced by the sum of (a) costs relating to the sale, (b) federal and state income taxes as a result of the sale, and (c) the amount used by the Company to pay in whole or in part financial institution debts secured by a mortgage of the Company s or any subsidiary s real property regardless of whether such mortgage encumbers the property sold.

202947_13_ITEM7_P20_S3	Global s appraiser arrived at a value of $15,400,000 for the Facility.

202947_13_ITEM7_P20_S5	Absent agreement amongst the three appraisers, the Appraised Value will be the average of the two appraisals that are closest to one another.
202947_13_ITEM7_P20_S6	Upon the determination of the Appraised Value, Global has the right to either rescind the notice of preliminary exercise or elect to commence a feasibility study and inspection period.
202947_13_ITEM7_P20_S7	At any time during the 180-day period of the feasibility study and inspection, Global may elect to rescind its notice of preliminary exercise.
202947_13_ITEM7_P20_S8	If Global fails to do so, then the exercise becomes final subject to the usual and customary closing conditions and the parties have not less than 90 days nor more than 120 days to close the transaction.
202947_13_ITEM7_P20_S9	However, the Company may, at its sole discretion, delay the closing for a period not to exceed twelve months.
202947_13_ITEM7_P21_S0	Under the Option Agreement, if Global elects to proceed with the purchase, it must pay the greater of (a) the Adjusted Book Value or (b) the Appraised Value.

202947_13_ITEM8_P0_S1	We have audited the accompanying consolidated balance sheets of Capital Properties, Inc. and subsidiaries as of December 31, 2012 and 2011, and the related consolidated statements of income, shareholders equity, and cash flows for the years then ended.
202947_13_ITEM8_P0_S2	These consolidated financial statements are the responsibility of the Company s management.
202947_13_ITEM8_P0_S3	Our responsibility is to express an opinion on these consolidated financial statements based on our audits.
202947_13_ITEM8_P0_S4	We conducted our audits in accordance with the standards of the Public Company Accounting Oversight Board (United States).
202947_13_ITEM8_P0_S5	Those standards require that we plan and perform the audit to obtain reasonable assurance about whether the consolidated financial statements are free of material misstatement.
202947_13_ITEM8_P0_S6	The Company is not required to have, nor were we engaged to perform, an audit of its internal control over financial reporting.
202947_13_ITEM8_P0_S7	An audit includes consideration of internal control over financial reporting as a basis for designing audit procedures that are appropriate in the circumstances, but not for the purpose of expressing an opinion on the effectiveness of the Company s internal control over financial reporting.
202947_13_ITEM8_P0_S8	Accordingly, we express no such opinion.
202947_13_ITEM8_P1_S0	An audit also includes examining, on a test basis, evidence supporting the amounts and disclosures in the consolidated financial statements, assessing the accounting principles used and significant estimates made by management and evaluating the overall financial statement presentation.
202947_13_ITEM8_P1_S1	We believe that our audits provide a reasonable basis for our opinion.
202947_13_ITEM8_P1_S2	In our opinion, the consolidated financial statements referred to above present fairly, in all material respects, the financial position of Capital Properties, Inc. and subsidiaries as of December 31, 2012 and 2011, and the results of their operations and their cash flows for the years then ended, in conformity with generally accepted accounting principles in the United States of America.

202947_13_ITEM8_P6_S0	Description of business: Capital Properties, Inc. and its wholly-owned subsidiaries, Tri-State Displays, Inc., Capital Terminal Company and Dunellen, LLC (collectively referred to as the Company ) operate in two segments, leasing and petroleum storage.
202947_13_ITEM8_P7_S0	The leasing segment consists of the long-term leasing of certain of its real estate interests in downtown Providence, Rhode Island (upon the commencement of which the tenants are required to construct buildings thereon, with the exception of the parking garage and Parcels 6B and 6C), the leasing of a portion of its building ( Steeple Street Building ) under short-term leasing arrangements and the leasing of locations along interstate and primary highways in Rhode Island and Massachusetts to Lamar Outdoor Advertising, LLC ( Lamar ) which has constructed outdoor advertising boards thereon.
202947_13_ITEM8_P7_S1	The Company anticipates that the future development of its remaining properties in and adjacent to the Capital Center area will consist primarily of long-term ground leases.
202947_13_ITEM8_P7_S2	Pending this development, the Company leases these parcels for public parking under short-term leasing arrangements to Metropark, Ltd. ( Metropark ).
202947_13_ITEM8_P8_S0	The petroleum storage segment consists of operating the petroleum storage terminal (the Terminal ) and the Wilkesbarre Pier (the Pier ), both of which are owned by the Company and are collectively referred to as the Facility, located in East Providence, Rhode Island, for Global Companies, LLC ( Global ) which stores and distributes petroleum products.
202947_13_ITEM8_P8_S1	The principal difference between the two segments relates to the nature of the operations.
202947_13_ITEM8_P9_S0	In the leasing segment, the tenants under long-term land leases incur substantially all of the development and operating costs of the assets constructed on the Company s land, including the payment of real property taxes on both the land and any improvements constructed thereon.
202947_13_ITEM8_P9_S1	In the petroleum storage segment, the Company is responsible for the operating and maintenance expenditures, including insurance and a portion of the real property taxes, as well as certain capital improvements at the Facility.
202947_13_ITEM8_P10_S0	Principles of consolidation: The accompanying consolidated financial statements include the accounts and transactions of the Company and its subsidiaries.
202947_13_ITEM8_P10_S1	All significant intercompany accounts and transactions have been eliminated in consolidation.
202947_13_ITEM8_P11_S0	Use of estimates: The preparation of consolidated financial statements in conformity with United States generally accepted accounting principles ( GAAP ) requires management to make estimates and assumptions that affect the reported amounts of assets and liabilities and disclosure of contingent assets and liabilities at the date of the financial statements.
202947_13_ITEM8_P11_S1	Estimates also affect the reported amounts of income and expenses during the reporting period.
202947_13_ITEM8_P11_S2	Actual results could differ from those estimates.
202947_13_ITEM8_P12_S0	Fair value of financial instruments: The Company believes that the fair values of its financial instruments, including cash, receivables and payables, approximate their respective book values because of their short-term nature.
202947_13_ITEM8_P12_S1	The fair value of the bank note payable approximates its book value and was determined using borrowing rates currently available to the Company for loans with similar terms and maturities.
202947_13_ITEM8_P12_S2	Based upon an opinion obtained by the Company from an investment banking firm, the fair value of the dividend notes payable approximates their book value.
202947_13_ITEM8_P12_S3	The fair values described herein were determined using significant other observable inputs (Level 2) as defined by GAAP.
202947_13_ITEM8_P13_S0	Properties and equipment: Properties and equipment are stated at cost.
202947_13_ITEM8_P13_S1	Acquisitions and additions are capitalized while routine maintenance and repairs, which do not improve the asset or extend its life, are charged to expense when incurred.
202947_13_ITEM8_P13_S2	Depreciation is being provided by the straight-line method over the estimated useful lives of the respective assets.
202947_13_ITEM8_P14_S0	The Company follows GAAP when accounting for the impairment or disposal of long-lived assets, which requires that properties and equipment held and used by the Company be reviewed for impairment whenever events or changes in circumstances indicate that the net book value of the asset may not be recoverable.
202947_13_ITEM8_P14_S1	An impairment loss will be recognized if the sum of the expected future cash flows (undiscounted and before interest) from the use of the asset is less than the net book value of the asset.
202947_13_ITEM8_P14_S2	Generally, the amount of the impairment loss is measured as the difference between the net book value and the estimated fair value of the asset.
202947_13_ITEM8_P15_S0	Cash and cash equivalents: The Company considers all highly liquid investments with a maturity of three months or less when purchased to be cash equivalents.
202947_13_ITEM8_P15_S1	At December 31, 2012 and 2011, the Company had no cash equivalents.
202947_13_ITEM8_P15_S2	The Company maintains all of its cash in non-interest bearing checking accounts in one bank which were fully insured by the Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation ( FDIC ).
202947_13_ITEM8_P15_S3	Effective January 1, 2013, the FDIC reduced the insurance on all non-interest bearing bank accounts to a maximum of $250,000.
202947_13_ITEM8_P16_S0	Environmental incidents: The Company accrues a liability when an environmental incident has occurred and the costs are estimable.
202947_13_ITEM8_P16_S1	The Company does not record a receivable for recoveries from third parties for environmental matters until it has determined that the amount of the collection is reasonably assured.
202947_13_ITEM8_P16_S2	The accrued liability is relieved when the Company pays the liability or a third party assumes the liability.
202947_13_ITEM8_P16_S3	Upon determination that collection is reasonably assured or a third party assumes the liability, the Company records the amount as a reduction of expense.
202947_13_ITEM8_P17_S0	The Company charges to expense those costs that do not extend the life, increase the capacity or improve the safety or efficiency of the property owned or used by the Company.
202947_13_ITEM8_P18_S0	Revenues: Leasing The Company s properties leased to others are under operating leases.
202947_13_ITEM8_P18_S1	The Company reports leasing revenue when earned under the operating method.
202947_13_ITEM8_P18_S2	Certain of the Company s long-term land leases, including the outdoor advertising locations, provide for presently known scheduled rent increases over the remaining terms (21 to 142 years).
202947_13_ITEM8_P18_S3	The Company follows GAAP in accounting for leases by recognizing leasing revenue on the straight-line basis over the terms of the leases; however, the Company does not report as revenue that portion of such straight-line rentals which management is unable to conclude is realizable (collectible) due to the length of the lease terms and other related uncertainties.
202947_13_ITEM8_P19_S0	Petroleum storage facility The Company reports revenue from the operations of the Facility when earned and reports as revenue the tenant s portion of the real property taxes and certain other items as required by the lease.
202947_13_ITEM8_P19_S1	Contingent The Company reports contingent revenue in the period in which the factors occur on which the contingent payments are predicated.
202947_13_ITEM8_P20_S0	Income taxes: The Company and its subsidiaries file consolidated income tax returns.
202947_13_ITEM8_P20_S1	The Company provides for income taxes based on income reported for financial reporting purposes.
202947_13_ITEM8_P20_S2	The provision for income taxes differs from the amounts currently payable because of temporary differences associated with the recognition of certain income and expense items for financial reporting and tax reporting purposes.
202947_13_ITEM8_P20_S3	The Company follows GAAP in accounting for uncertainty in income taxes.
202947_13_ITEM8_P20_S4	Based on its evaluation, the Company has concluded that there are no significant uncertain tax positions requiring recognition in the consolidated financial statements.
202947_13_ITEM8_P20_S5	The Company will report any tax-related interest and penalties related to uncertain tax positions as a component of income tax expense.
202947_13_ITEM8_P21_S0	Legal fees: The Company recognizes legal fees as incurred.
202947_13_ITEM8_P22_S0	Basic earnings per common share: Basic earnings per common share are computed by dividing net income by the weighted average number of common shares outstanding during the period.

202947_13_ITEM8_P31_S0	Description of leasing arrangements: Long-term land leases: As of December 31, 2012, the Company had entered into nine long-term land leases, including the Parcel 6A lease discussed below.
202947_13_ITEM8_P31_S1	Of the nine parcels, seven have had improvements constructed thereon.
202947_13_ITEM8_P31_S2	Under the nine land leases, the tenants are required to negotiate any tax stabilization treaty or other arrangements, appeal any changes in real property assessments, and pay real property taxes assessed on land and improvements under these arrangements.
202947_13_ITEM8_P31_S3	Accordingly, real property taxes payable by the tenants are excluded from leasing revenues and leasing expenses on the accompanying consolidated statements of income.

202947_13_ITEM8_P40_S0	Petroleum storage facility and environmental incidents: Exercise of purchase option by Global: Since 1998, the Company and Global have been parties to a lease agreement whereby the Company operates the entire Facility for Global.

202947_13_ITEM8_P42_S0	Under the terms of the Option Agreement between the Company and Global dated June 9, 2003 (the Option Agreement ), on April 27, 2012, Global preliminarily exercised its option to purchase the Company s Facility.
202947_13_ITEM8_P42_S1	In compliance with the Option Agreement, the Company thereafter provided Global with a calculation of Adjusted Book Value (as that term is defined in the Option Agreement) of the Facility which amounted to $19,700,000.

202947_13_ITEM8_P43_S0	Global and the Company each selected an appraiser.

202947_13_ITEM8_P43_S3	Global s appraiser arrived at a value of $15,400,000 for the Facility.
202947_13_ITEM8_P43_S4	As required by the Option Agreement, the two appraisers then engaged a third appraiser whose appraisal is expected to be completed on or before March 31, 2013.
202947_13_ITEM8_P43_S5	Absent agreement amongst the three appraisers, the Appraised Value will be the average of the two appraisals that are closest to one another.
202947_13_ITEM8_P43_S6	Upon the determination of the Appraised Value, Global has the right to either rescind the notice of preliminary exercise or elect to commence a feasibility study and inspection period.
202947_13_ITEM8_P43_S7	At any time during the 180-day period of the feasibility study and inspection, Global may elect to rescind its notice of preliminary exercise.
202947_13_ITEM8_P43_S8	If Global fails to do so, then the exercise becomes final subject to the usual and customary closing conditions and the parties have not less than 90 days nor more than 120 days to close the transaction.
202947_13_ITEM8_P43_S9	However, the Company may, at its sole discretion, delay the closing for a period not to exceed twelve months.
202947_13_ITEM8_P44_S0	Under the Option Agreement, if Global elects to proceed with the purchase, it must pay the greater of (a) the Adjusted Book Value or (b) the Appraised Value.

202947_13_ITEM8_P45_S0	The Pier is a deep-water pier in East Providence, Rhode Island owned by the Company which is integral to the operation of the Terminal.

202947_13_ITEM8_P46_S0	On August 31, 2011, while excavating in connection with the construction of a highway for the Rhode Island Department of Transportation ( RIDOT ), Cardi Corporation ( Cardi ) ruptured an underground pipeline controlled and used by the Company for the transportation of ULSD from the Wilkesbarre Pier to its Petroleum Storage Facility.
202947_13_ITEM8_P46_S1	At the time, the Company was receiving product from a barge and, as a result of the rupture, approximately 70,000 gallons of ULSD were discharged.
202947_13_ITEM8_P47_S0	Pursuant to the Company s Emergency Response Plan, representatives of the Company took control of the spill site and coordinated the response of various governmental agencies as well as private contractors.
202947_13_ITEM8_P47_S1	Approximately 56,000 gallons of spilled diesel were recovered.
202947_13_ITEM8_P47_S2	On September 6, 2011, the Company turned over the responsibility for the cleanup to Cardi.
202947_13_ITEM8_P47_S3	The Company notified the required government agencies and its insurance carriers of the rupture.
202947_13_ITEM8_P47_S4	Management s estimate of the total cost incurred by the Company in responding to the emergency and repairing the pipeline was $349,000, which amount was accrued as an expense at September 30, 2011, and the Company determined that no receivable could be recorded at that time.
202947_13_ITEM8_P47_S5	In November 2011, Cardi paid the Company $89,000, which amount was offset against the expense previously recorded.
202947_13_ITEM8_P47_S6	During the fourth quarter of 2011, the Company paid an additional $14,000 in connection with the pipeline rupture.
202947_13_ITEM8_P47_S7	At December 31, 2011, the Company determined that $184,000 of the remaining liability was assumed by Cardi.
202947_13_ITEM8_P47_S8	The Company reduced the previously recorded liability and expense by that amount.
202947_13_ITEM8_P47_S9	In February 2012, Cardi paid the $184,000.
202947_13_ITEM8_P47_S10	In May 2012, Cardi paid both the remaining $76,000 and the $14,000, and the Company reduced the accrued liability and recorded the $90,000 as a reduction of expense on the accompanying consolidated statement of income for the year ended December 31, 2012.
202947_13_ITEM8_P48_S0	In March 2011, management learned that, during the normal receipt of product from a barge, No. 2 heating oil (high sulfur heating oil) was accidentally pumped into one of the Company s ULSD petroleum storage tanks (Tank 67), resulting in a mixture with a sulfur content in excess of that allowed by the Environmental Protection Agency ( EPA ).
202947_13_ITEM8_P48_S1	The Company notified Global and its insurance carriers of the incident.
202947_13_ITEM8_P49_S0	Global informed the Company that it had contacted its customers that received the mixture and commenced a sampling and testing program with certain of its customers to determine (1) if any product should be removed and replaced with conforming product or (2) if the product need only be treated to meet the EPA requirements.
202947_13_ITEM8_P50_S0	In August 2011, Global asserted a claim against the Company of $132,000 for damages incurred by Global arising out of the incident, which amount was accrued as an expense at September 30, 2011.
202947_13_ITEM8_P50_S1	At December 31, 2011, the Company determined that its insurance carrier had assumed this liability, and the Company reduced the previously recorded liability and expense by that amount.
202947_13_ITEM8_P50_S2	In March 2012, the Company s insurance carrier paid Global the full amount of its claim, and Global released the Company of all liability relating to this incident.
202947_13_ITEM8_P51_S0	In August 2010, during a regular facility inspection of the Terminal, a release of petroleum-contaminated water was discovered from the tank bottom of one of the Company s 150,000 barrel tanks (Tank 153).
202947_13_ITEM8_P51_S1	The Company notified the Rhode Island Department of Environmental Management ( RIDEM ), the EPA and the United States Coast Guard.
202947_13_ITEM8_P51_S2	It also notified its insurance carriers of the release and the damage to the tank.
202947_13_ITEM8_P51_S3	The tank was emptied of product and the cleaning of the tank bottom was completed in September 2010.
202947_13_ITEM8_P51_S4	The petroleum-contaminated water released from the tank was contained on the secondary containment liner under the tank bottom, preventing contamination of the groundwater.
202947_13_ITEM8_P51_S5	The Company engaged an outside engineering firm to inspect the tank bottom to determine the cause and location of the release, as well as the extent of the required repairs.
202947_13_ITEM8_P51_S6	The findings of the inspection indicated that aggressive corrosion from inside the tank occurred, causing two holes in the immediate vicinity of the observed release, as well as several other holes or potential holes in other areas of the tank bottom.
202947_13_ITEM8_P51_S7	The report concluded that the corrosion was caused by microbial contamination, which was affirmed by a corrosion specialist.
202947_13_ITEM8_P51_S8	The final cost of the cleanup, inspection and repair of the tank was $533,000, all of which was recorded as an expense at December 31, 2010.
202947_13_ITEM8_P51_S9	The tank was placed back in service in February 2011.
202947_13_ITEM8_P51_S10	In June 2011, Global paid the Company $458,000 which is recorded in petroleum storage facility revenues, reimbursement of tank repairs on the accompanying consolidated statement of income for the year ended December 31, 2011.
202947_13_ITEM8_P51_S11	The difference relates to the $75,000 cost of epoxy coating the bottom of Tank 153 which the Company paid.
202947_13_ITEM8_P52_S0	The testing of certain of the Company s other tanks revealed the presence of corrosive microbial contaminants in Tanks 151 and 32.
202947_13_ITEM8_P52_S1	Both tanks were treated with a biocide and continue to be monitored and treated as necessary.
202947_13_ITEM8_P52_S2	Since Tank 32 had been inspected in June 2010, the Company believes that the contaminants have not affected the integrity of this tank bottom.
202947_13_ITEM8_P52_S3	However, since Tank 151 had not been inspected since construction in 2006, the Company took this tank out of service in February 2011.
202947_13_ITEM8_P52_S4	The tank was emptied of product, and an inspection of the tank bottom revealed minor corrosion.
202947_13_ITEM8_P52_S5	The Company completed the repairs recommended by the inspectors and applied an epoxy coating to the bottom of Tank 151 at a cost of $50,000, which has been included in petroleum storage facility expenses, operating on the accompanying consolidated statement of income for the year ended December 31, 2011.
202947_13_ITEM8_P52_S6	The tank was back in service in May 2011.
202947_13_ITEM8_P52_S7	Exclusive of the epoxy coating, the total cost of cleanup, inspection and repair of Tanks 151 and 32 was $40,000 which Global paid the Company in September 2011 and is recorded in petroleum storage facilities revenues, reimbursement of tank repairs on the accompanying consolidated statement of income for the year ended December 31, 2011.
202947_13_ITEM8_P52_S8	Tank repairs related to this incident have been presented as a separate line item within petroleum storage facility expenses on the accompanying consolidated statement of income for the year ended December 31, 2011.
202947_13_ITEM8_P52_S9	Routine tank repairs continue to be included with petroleum storage facility operating expenses on the accompanying consolidated statements of income.
202947_13_ITEM8_P53_S0	Environmental incident (2002): In 2002, during testing of monitoring wells at the Terminal, the Company s consulting engineer discovered free floating phase product in a groundwater monitoring well located on that portion of the Terminal purchased in 2000.
202947_13_ITEM8_P53_S1	Laboratory analysis indicated that the product was gasoline, which is not a product the Company ever stored at the Terminal.
202947_13_ITEM8_P53_S2	The Company commenced an environmental investigation and analysis, the results of which indicate that the gasoline did not come from the Terminal.
202947_13_ITEM8_P53_S3	RIDEM subsequently identified Power Test Realty Partnership ( Power Test ), the owner of an adjacent parcel, as a potentially responsible party for the contamination.
202947_13_ITEM8_P53_S4	Getty Properties Corp. is the general partner of Power Test.
202947_13_ITEM8_P54_S0	Power Test challenged that determination and, after an administrative hearing, in October 2008 a RIDEM Hearing Officer determined that Power Test is responsible for the discharge of the petroleum product under the Rhode Island Oil Pollution Control Act, R.I.G.L. Section 46-12.5.1-3 and Rule 6(a) and 12(b) of the Oil Pollution Control Regulations.
202947_13_ITEM8_P54_S1	The RIDEM Decision and Order requires Power Test to remediate the contamination as directed by RIDEM and remanded the proposed penalty to RIDEM for recalculation.
202947_13_ITEM8_P54_S2	In November 2008, Power Test appealed the decision to the Rhode Island Superior Court.
202947_13_ITEM8_P55_S0	Order of the Hearing Officer pending a clarification by RIDEM of the amount of the proposed penalty.
202947_13_ITEM8_P55_S1	In October 2009, RIDEM issued a recalculated administrative penalty, and, subsequently, the RIDEM Hearing Officer issued a recommended amended decision, which was affirmed as a final decision by the RIDEM Director in December 2009.
202947_13_ITEM8_P55_S2	In January 2010, Power Test appealed that decision to Superior Court.
202947_13_ITEM8_P55_S3	In September 2011, the Superior Court affirmed the decision of the RIDEM director.
202947_13_ITEM8_P55_S4	Power Test has appealed that decision to the Rhode Island Supreme Court.
202947_13_ITEM8_P56_S0	In April 2009, the Company sued Power Test and Getty Properties Corp. in the Rhode Island Superior Court seeking remediation of the site or, in the alternative, the cost of the remediation.
202947_13_ITEM8_P56_S1	On May 1, 2009, Power Test and Getty Properties Corp. removed the action to the United States District Court for the District of Rhode Island ( the Court ).
202947_13_ITEM8_P57_S0	On May 22, 2009, Power Test and Getty Properties Corp. answered the Complaint and filed a Counterclaim against Dunellen, LLC and Capital Terminal Company alleging that Dunellen, LLC and Capital Terminal Company are responsible for the contamination.
202947_13_ITEM8_P57_S1	Getty Properties Corp. and Power Test joined Getty Petroleum Marketing, Inc., the tenant under a long-term lease with Getty Properties Corp. of the adjacent property, as a defendant.
202947_13_ITEM8_P57_S2	The Company amended its Complaint to add Getty Petroleum Marketing, Inc. as a defendant.
202947_13_ITEM8_P57_S3	Getty Petroleum Marketing, Inc. moved for summary judgment against the Company, Getty Properties Corp. and Power Test.
202947_13_ITEM8_P58_S0	On December 5, 2011, Getty Petroleum Marketing, Inc. filed for bankruptcy under Chapter 11 of the United States Bankruptcy Act.
202947_13_ITEM8_P58_S1	Thereafter, with Bankruptcy Court approval, Getty Petroleum Marketing, Inc. rejected its lease with Getty Properties Corp.
202947_13_ITEM8_P58_S2	On August 24, 2012, the Bankruptcy Court approved a plan to liquidate Getty Petroleum Marketing, Inc.
202947_13_ITEM8_P58_S3	On January 15, 2013, the Court granted Getty Petroleum Marketing, Inc. s motion for summary judgment against the Company, Getty Properties Corp. and Power Test, dismissing the Company s third-party complaint.
202947_13_ITEM8_P58_S4	The parties are awaiting a scheduling order from the Court.
202947_13_ITEM8_P58_S5	There can be no assurance that the Company will prevail in this litigation.
202947_13_ITEM8_P58_S6	Since January 2003, the Company has not incurred significant costs in connection with this matter, other than ongoing litigation costs, and is unable to determine the costs it might incur to remedy the situation, as well as any costs to investigate, defend and seek reimbursement from the responsible party with respect to this contamination.
202947_13_ITEM8_P59_S0	In 1994, a leak was discovered in a 25,000 barrel storage tank at the Terminal which allowed the escape of a small amount of fuel oil.
202947_13_ITEM8_P59_S1	All required notices were made to RIDEM.
202947_13_ITEM8_P59_S2	In 2000, the tank was demolished and testing of the groundwater indicated that there was no large pooling of contaminants.
202947_13_ITEM8_P60_S0	In 2001, RIDEM approved a plan pursuant to which the Company installed a passive system consisting of three wells and commenced monitoring the wells.
202947_13_ITEM8_P60_S1	In 2003, RIDEM decided that the passive monitoring system previously approved was not sufficient and required the Company to design an active remediation system for the removal of product from the contaminated site.
202947_13_ITEM8_P60_S2	The Company and its consulting engineers began the pre-design testing of the site in the fourth quarter of 2004.
202947_13_ITEM8_P60_S3	The consulting engineers estimated a total cost of $200,000 to design, install and operate the system, which amount was accrued in 2004.
202947_13_ITEM8_P60_S4	Through 2006, the Company had expended $119,000 and has not incurred any additional costs since then.
202947_13_ITEM8_P60_S5	In 2011, RIDEM notified the company to proceed with the next phase of the approval process, notifying the abutters of the proposed remediation system even though RIDEM has not yet taken any action on the Company s proposed plan.
202947_13_ITEM8_P61_S0	As designed, the system will pump out the contaminants which will be disposed of in compliance with applicable regulations.
202947_13_ITEM8_P61_S1	After a period of time, the groundwater will be tested to determine if sufficient contaminants have been removed.
202947_13_ITEM8_P61_S2	While the Company and its consulting engineers believe that the proposed active remediation system will correct the situation, it is possible that RIDEM could require the Company to expand remediation efforts, which could result in the Company incurring costs in excess of the remaining accrual of $81,000.

202947_13_ITEM8_P66_S0	In November 2008, the Company restated its Articles of Incorporation:
202947_13_ITEM8_P67_S0	To provide for certain transfer and ownership restrictions as set forth therein.
202947_13_ITEM8_P68_S0	In December 2008, the Company issued (in the form of a stock dividend) 3,299,956 shares of Class B Common Stock on a one-for-one basis for each share of Class A Common Stock held.
202947_13_ITEM8_P68_S1	The holders of Class A and Class B Common Stock vote together as a single class on all matters submitted to the shareholders of the Company except for the election of the Board of Directors and except in connection with certain major corporate actions, including a sale of the Company.
202947_13_ITEM8_P68_S2	The holders of Class A Common Stock, voting as a separate class, elect one-third of the Board of Directors.
202947_13_ITEM8_P68_S3	The holders of Class B Common Stock, voting as a separate class, elect the remainder of the Board of Directors.
202947_13_ITEM8_P68_S4	Class B Common Stock is convertible by the record owner thereof into the same number of shares of Class A Common Stock at any time.
202947_13_ITEM8_P68_S5	For the years ended December 31, 2012 and 2011, the number of shares converted was 45,586 shares and 16,318 shares, respectively.
202947_13_ITEM8_P69_S0	The Class A Common Stock is listed on the Premier QX Tier of the OTCQX.
202947_13_ITEM8_P69_S1	The Class B Common Stock is not listed on any national or regional stock exchange, or on the National Association of Securities Dealers Automated Quotation National Market System or on the OTCQX.
202947_13_ITEM8_P70_S0	The holders of Class A and Class B Common Stock share equally in the earnings of the Company and in dividends declared by the Company.
202947_13_ITEM8_P71_S0	The Company s Restated Articles of Incorporation prohibits any shareholder from acquiring more than a 5% interest in the Company s classes of common stock and prohibits any shareholder or any beneficial owner who, at the time of the filing of the Restated Articles of Incorporation owned 5% or more of the Company s classes of common stock from increasing their aggregate percentage ownership of both classes of common stock.
202947_13_ITEM8_P71_S1	Should a shareholder acquire a number of shares that results in the limitation being exceeded, shares in excess of the limitation would be automatically converted into an equal number of shares of Excess Stock, which class was authorized pursuant to the 2001 Amendment to the Company s Articles of Incorporation.
202947_13_ITEM8_P71_S2	Excess Stock is non-voting and is not entitled to dividends.
202947_13_ITEM8_P71_S3	However, the shareholder may designate a qualifying transferee for shares of Excess Stock, at which time such shares would be converted and reissued as Class A or Class B Common shares as the case may be.
202947_13_ITEM8_P72_S0	The purpose for creating the Class B Common Stock was to put the Company in the position to qualify to be taxed as a real estate investment trust ( REIT ).
202947_13_ITEM8_P72_S1	One of the qualifications to be taxed as a REIT is that no more than 50% of the shares of a company can be held by five or fewer individuals during the last half of each taxable year.
202947_13_ITEM8_P72_S2	Currently, the majority shareholder controls 52.3% of the Company s outstanding common stock and three other shareholders each own more than 5% of the Company s outstanding common stock.
202947_13_ITEM8_P72_S3	In order for the Company to qualify to be taxed as a REIT, the major shareholders ownership of the Company s issued and outstanding common stock would need to be reduced below the 50% level.
202947_13_ITEM8_P72_S4	On January 29, 2013, the Board of Directors of the Company approved submitting to the shareholders at the 2013 annual meeting Amended and Restated Articles of Incorporation which, among other things, would eliminate the Class B Common shares and automatically convert all Class B Common shares into an equivalent number of Class A Common shares, and all restrictions that presently exist with respect to the ownership of Class A and Class B Common stock would be eliminated.
202947_13_ITEM8_P72_S5	The Board took this action after concluding that conversion to a REIT was unlikely to occur at any time in the foreseeable future.
202947_13_ITEM8_P72_S6	On December 7, 2012, the Company s Board of Directors declared a dividend of $2.25 per share ($14,850,000) to shareholders of record as of December 17, 2012.
202947_13_ITEM8_P72_S7	For shareholders owning 100 or more shares, the dividend was payable 20%, or $.45 per share, in cash and 80%, or $1.80 per share, in Dividend Notes to be issued by the Company.
202947_13_ITEM8_P72_S8	Shareholders owning less than 100 shares of any class of Company stock where the shares were titled in their names and not held by a broker, received 100% of the dividend in cash unless they elected to receive it 20% in cash and 80% in Dividend Notes.
202947_13_ITEM8_P72_S9	The dividend was paid on December 27, 2012, at which time the Company paid out $3,063,000 in cash, and issued $11,787,000 in 5% Dividend Notes described in Note 4 above.
202947_13_ITEM8_P72_S10	In accordance with GAAP, at December 7, 2012, the Company s retained earnings of $3,870,000 was reduced to zero and the remaining $10,980,000 was offset against capital in excess of par.
202947_13_ITEM8_P72_S11	In connection with the declaration of the dividend, the Company s Board of Directors received a solvency opinion from an investment banking firm to the effect that the dividend would not result in the Company s liabilities exceeding its assets and would not render the Company insolvent.

202947_13_ITEM8_P76_S0	Related party transaction: The Company and Providence and Worcester Railroad Company ( the Railroad ) have a common controlling shareholder.
202947_13_ITEM8_P77_S0	The Company has the right to use certain pipelines located in the right of way of the Railroad which were constructed by Getty Oil Company (Eastern Operations), Inc. ( GettyEO ).
202947_13_ITEM8_P77_S1	Pursuant to an agreement between the Railroad and GettyEO dated August 6, 1975, the Railroad has the right to relocate any portion of the pipelines located within the Railroad s right of way.
202947_13_ITEM8_P78_S0	The Company supported the extension of Waterfront Drive, so-called, up to Dexter Road and adjacent to the Company s Terminal, which road was constructed on the Railroad right of way.
202947_13_ITEM8_P78_S1	The road was completed in November 2012.
202947_13_ITEM8_P79_S0	The State of Rhode Island s plans for the Waterfront Drive extension required a relocation of a portion of the pipelines which the Railroad had the right to relocate.
202947_13_ITEM8_P79_S1	RIDOT entered into an agreement with the Railroad (the RIDOT Agreement ) to reimburse the Railroad for reasonable costs incurred by it in relocating the pipelines, which were originally estimated to be $159,000.
202947_13_ITEM8_P79_S2	Any substantial change to the estimate requires the approval of RIDOT.
202947_13_ITEM8_P80_S0	In May 2011, the Company entered into an agreement with the Railroad to act as the Railroad s agent with respect to the relocation of the pipelines.
202947_13_ITEM8_P80_S1	The Company, without receiving compensation, is obligated under the agreement to select, direct and supervise all subcontractors subject to the Railroad s approval.
202947_13_ITEM8_P81_S0	Upon the Railroad s receipt of invoices from the contractors, the Railroad requires the Company to verify the accuracy of the invoices and submit a check to the Railroad covering the amount of the invoices.
202947_13_ITEM8_P81_S1	The Railroad pays the invoices, using the funds advanced by the Company.
202947_13_ITEM8_P81_S2	The Railroad is then obligated to submit the invoices to RIDOT for reimbursement.
202947_13_ITEM8_P81_S3	Any reimbursements received by the Railroad from RIDOT are required to be paid to the Company in a timely manner.
202947_13_ITEM8_P81_S4	Any shortfall in RIDOT s reimbursement is borne by the Company.
202947_13_ITEM8_P81_S5	At December 31, 2011, costs incurred to relocate the pipeline totaled $219,000, which amount is included in prepaid and other on the accompanying consolidated balance sheet at December 31, 2011.
202947_13_ITEM8_P81_S6	The Railroad submitted the total amount to RIDOT in February 2012; in March and December 2012, RIDOT reimbursed the Railroad a total of $198,000, which the Railroad in turn paid to the Company.
202947_13_ITEM8_P81_S7	RIDOT has retained the remaining $21,000 pending its audit of the project, which amount is included in prepaid and other on the accompanying consolidated balance sheet at December 31, 2012.
202947_13_ITEM8_P81_S8	The Company believes the remaining $21,000 will ultimately be paid.

202947_13_ITEM9A_P1_S0	The Company s management is responsible for establishing and maintaining adequate internal control over financial reporting (as such term is defined in Rules 13a-15(f) and 15d-15(f) under the Exchange Act).
202947_13_ITEM9A_P1_S1	The Company s internal control over financial reporting is designed to provide reasonable assurance regarding the reliability of its financial reporting and the preparation of published financial statements in accordance with United States generally accepted accounting principles.
202947_13_ITEM9A_P1_S2	However, because of its inherent limitations, internal control over financial reporting may not prevent or detect misstatements.
202947_13_ITEM9A_P1_S3	Therefore, even those systems determined to be effective can provide only reasonable assurance with respect to financial statement preparation and presentation.
202947_13_ITEM9A_P1_S4	Also, projections of any evaluation of effectiveness to future periods are subject to the risk that controls may become inadequate because of changes in conditions, or the degree of compliance with policies may deteriorate.
202947_13_ITEM9A_P2_S0	Management conducted its evaluation of the effectiveness of its internal control over financial reporting based on the framework in Internal Control-Integrated Framework issued by the Committee of Sponsoring Organizations of the Treadway Commission ( COSO ) as of December 31, 2012.
202947_13_ITEM9A_P2_S1	Based on this assessment, the principal executive officer and principal financial officer believe that as of December 31, 2012, the Company s internal control over financial reporting was effective based on criteria set forth by COSO in Internal Control-Integrated Framework.
202947_13_ITEM9A_P2_S2	This annual report does not include an attestation report of the Company s independent registered public accounting firm regarding internal control over financial reporting.

202947_14_ITEM1_P0_S0	under the laws of Rhode Island in 1983 as Providence and Worcester Company and is the successor by merger in 1983 to a corporation also named Providence and Worcester Company which was organized under the laws of Delaware in 1979.
202947_14_ITEM1_P0_S1	In 1984, the Company s name was changed to Capital Properties, Inc.

202947_14_ITEM1_P2_S0	Segments The Company operates in two segments: leasing and petroleum storage.
202947_14_ITEM1_P2_S1	For financial information, see Note 9 of Notes to Consolidated Financial Statements in Item 8.
202947_14_ITEM1_P3_S0	The leasing segment is principally devoted to the leasing of Company-owned land in the Capital Center area ( Capital Center ) in downtown Providence, Rhode Island under long-term ground leases.
202947_14_ITEM1_P3_S1	The Company owns approximately 18 acres in the Capital Center consisting of 13 individual parcels.
202947_14_ITEM1_P4_S0	The Capital Center (approximately 77 acres of land) is the result of a development project undertaken by the State of Rhode Island, the City of Providence, the National Railroad Passenger Corporation ( Amtrak ) and the Company during the 1980 s in which two rivers, the Moshassuck and the Woonasquatucket, were moved, Amtrak s Northeast Corridor rail line was relocated, a new Amtrak/commuter railroad station was constructed and significant public improvements were made to improve pedestrian and vehicular traffic in the area.
202947_14_ITEM1_P5_S0	With the exception of the Steeple Street property, the Company has not acted, and does not intend to act, as a developer with respect to any improvements constructed on Company-owned parcels.
202947_14_ITEM1_P5_S1	Rather, the Company offers individual parcels for lease pursuant to long-term ground leases with terms of 99 years or more.
202947_14_ITEM1_P5_S2	Each lease contains provisions permitting the tenant to develop the parcel under certain terms and conditions.
202947_14_ITEM1_P5_S3	Each lease provides for periodic rent adjustments of various kinds.
202947_14_ITEM1_P6_S0	Under the leases, the tenants are responsible for insuring the Company against various hazards and events.
202947_14_ITEM1_P6_S1	Each tenant is required to indemnify the Company with respect to all of the tenant s activities on the land.
202947_14_ITEM1_P6_S2	The leases contain other terms and conditions customary to such instruments.
202947_14_ITEM1_P7_S0	The Company first began offering parcels for lease in the Capital Center area in the late 1980 s.
202947_14_ITEM1_P7_S1	As of December 31, 2013, nine parcels have been leased by the Company under long-term leases of 99 years or more.
202947_14_ITEM1_P7_S2	Of the nine parcels, seven have improvements constructed thereon as follows:
202947_14_ITEM1_P8_S0	While seeking developers, the Company also leases Parcels 3E, 3W, 4E and 4W in the Capital Center area for public parking purposes on a short-term basis to Metropark, Ltd.
202947_14_ITEM1_P9_S0	Parcel 20 Adjacent to the Capital Center Since the 1980 s, the Company has owned an undeveloped parcel of land adjacent to the Capital Center, which is leased out for public parking purposes on a short-term basis.
202947_14_ITEM1_P9_S1	In 2007, the Company purchased the adjacent parcel containing a three/four-story 18,000 square foot building (the Steeple Street Building ) and related land for $2,329,000, which, together with the previously-owned land, now comprises Parcel 20, containing 26,600 square feet.
202947_14_ITEM1_P9_S2	The Steeple Street Building is on the State Registry of Historic Buildings.
202947_14_ITEM1_P9_S3	During 2010-11, the Company substantially rehabilitated the Building.
202947_14_ITEM1_P10_S0	The Building has three commercial tenants with additional space available for lease.
202947_14_ITEM1_P10_S1	All of the properties described above are shown on a map contained in Exhibit 20.1.
202947_14_ITEM1_P11_S0	Lamar Lease The Company, through a wholly-owned subsidiary, leases 23 outdoor advertising locations containing 44 billboard faces along interstate and primary highways in Rhode Island and Massachusetts to Lamar Outdoor Advertising, LLC ( Lamar ) under a lease which now expires in 2045.
202947_14_ITEM1_P11_S1	All but one of these locations are controlled by the Company through permanent easements granted to the Company pursuant to an agreement between the Company and Providence Worcester Railroad Company, a related company ( Railroad the remaining location is leased by the Company from a third party with a remaining term of eighteen months with an option to renew for an additional five years.
202947_14_ITEM1_P11_S2	Although no new locations have been added since 2002, in 2013 Lamar converted billboards at two locations to electronic boards, which conversions extended the term of the lease for a total of twelve years to 2045.
202947_14_ITEM1_P11_S3	Lamar has a right of first refusal for additional billboard location sites acquired by the Company in New England and Metropolitan New York City.
202947_14_ITEM1_P12_S0	The lease with Lamar provides, among other things, for the following: (1) the base rent will increase annually at the rate of 2.75% for each leased billboard location commencing June 1, 2006 and on each June 1 thereafter; and (2) in addition to base rent, for each 12-month period commencing each June 1, Lamar must pay to the Company 30% of the gross revenues from each standard billboard and 20% of the gross revenues from each electronic billboard for such 12-month period, reduced by the sum of (a) commissions paid to third parties and (b) the base monthly rent for each leased billboard display for such 12-month period.
202947_14_ITEM1_P12_S1	The Lamar lease contains other terms and conditions customary to such instruments.
202947_14_ITEM1_P13_S0	The Company has the right to require the Railroad to grant to it additional permanent easements for the location of billboards along the Railroad s right-of-way on commercially reasonable terms.

202947_14_ITEM1_P17_S0	Petroleum Storage Terminal and Pier Facility The Company, through its wholly-owned subsidiary, Dunellen, LLC, owns a petroleum storage terminal containing 1,004,000 shell barrels (the Terminal ) and the Wilkesbarre Pier (the Pier ), collectively referred to as the Facility, located in East Providence, Rhode Island.

202947_14_ITEM1_P18_S0	For the period May 1, 1998 to April 30, 2013, the Company leased the Facility to Global Companies, LLC ( Global ) for the storage and sale of petroleum distillates and operated the Facility for Global pursuant to a contract with another Company subsidiary, Capital Terminal Company.
202947_14_ITEM1_P18_S1	The Company was responsible for labor, insurance, a portion of the real property taxes and other operating expenses, as well as certain capital improvements.
202947_14_ITEM1_P19_S0	Under the terms of the Option Agreement between the Company and Global dated June 9, 2003 (the Option Agreement ), on April 27, 2012, Global preliminarily exercised its option to purchase the Company s Facility.
202947_14_ITEM1_P19_S1	In compliance with the Option Agreement, the Company thereafter provided Global with a calculation of Adjusted Book Value (as that term is defined in the Option Agreement) of the Facility, which amounted to $19,700,000.
202947_14_ITEM1_P19_S2	Global then elected to proceed with the determination of Appraised Value (as defined in the Option Agreement).
202947_14_ITEM1_P19_S3	Global and the Company each selected an appraiser and elected to defer selection of a third appraiser until their respective appraisers completed their appraisals and discussed the results.
202947_14_ITEM1_P19_S4	The Company s appraiser arrived at an appraised value of $46,200,000 for the Facility.
202947_14_ITEM1_P19_S5	Global s appraiser arrived at a value of $15,400,000 for the Facility.
202947_14_ITEM1_P19_S6	As required by the Option Agreement, the two appraisers then engaged a third appraiser who on May 17, 2013 appraised the Facility at $35,000,000.
202947_14_ITEM1_P19_S7	Global had ten business days following the receipt of the third appraisal to elect to proceed with a feasibility study of the Facility, which it failed to do.
202947_14_ITEM1_P19_S8	As a result, the Option Agreement terminated on June 3, 2013.
202947_14_ITEM1_P20_S0	Termination of Global Lease: On May 1, 2012, the Company gave Global notice of non-extension of the Global lease.
202947_14_ITEM1_P20_S1	Global was solely responsible for the removal of its inventory and the cleaning of the tanks prior to May 1, 2013 and the costs associated with these activities.
202947_14_ITEM1_P20_S2	The Global lease terminated on April 30, 2013, and the Company took full control of the Facility on that date.
202947_14_ITEM1_P21_S0	Prior to April 30, 2013, Global completed the removal of product and the cleaning of the tanks.
202947_14_ITEM1_P21_S1	The final inspection report indicated that two tanks required repairs, which repairs were done by the Company and the costs reimbursed by Global.
202947_14_ITEM1_P22_S0	Effective September 1, 2013, the Company entered into a through-put lease with Atlantic Trading Marketing, Inc. ( ATMI ) for 425,000 shell barrels for a term of eight months with automatic three-month extensions unless terminated by either party.
202947_14_ITEM1_P22_S1	In addition, the Company granted ATMI a month-to-month option to lease up to 220,000 additional barrels on an as-used basis.

202947_14_ITEM1_P25_S0	The operation of a petroleum storage facility carries with it the risk of environmental contamination.
202947_14_ITEM1_P26_S0	Pipeline rupture (2011): On August 31, 2011, while excavating in connection with the construction of a highway for the Rhode Island Department of Transportation ( RIDOT ), Cardi Corporation ( Cardi ) ruptured an underground pipeline controlled and used by the Company for the transportation of ULSD from the Wilkesbarre Pier to the Terminal.
202947_14_ITEM1_P26_S1	At the time, the Company was receiving product from a barge and, as a result of the rupture, approximately 70,000 gallons of ULSD were discharged.
202947_14_ITEM1_P27_S0	Pursuant to the Company s Emergency Response Plan, representatives of the Company took control of the spill site and coordinated the response of various governmental agencies as well as private contractors.
202947_14_ITEM1_P27_S1	Approximately 56,000 gallons of spilled diesel were recovered.
202947_14_ITEM1_P27_S2	On September 6, 2011, the Company turned over the responsibility for the cleanup to Cardi.
202947_14_ITEM1_P27_S3	The Company notified the required government agencies and its insurance carriers of the rupture.
202947_14_ITEM1_P27_S4	The total cost incurred by the Company in responding to the emergency and repairing the pipeline was $363,000.
202947_14_ITEM1_P27_S5	Cardi paid the Company as follows: $89,000 in November 2011, $184,000 in February 2012, and the balance of $90,000 in May 2012.
202947_14_ITEM1_P28_S0	Environmental incident (2002): In 2002, during testing of monitoring wells at the Terminal, the Company s consulting engineer discovered free floating phase product in a groundwater monitoring well located on that portion of the Terminal purchased in 2000.
202947_14_ITEM1_P29_S0	Company ever stored at the Terminal.
202947_14_ITEM1_P29_S1	The Company commenced an environmental investigation and analysis, the results of which indicate that the gasoline did not come from the Terminal.
202947_14_ITEM1_P29_S2	RIDEM subsequently identified Power Test Realty Partnership ( Power Test ), the owner of an adjacent parcel, as a potentially responsible party for the contamination.
202947_14_ITEM1_P29_S3	Getty Properties Corp. is the general partner of Power Test.
202947_14_ITEM1_P30_S0	Power Test challenged that determination and, after an administrative hearing, in October 2008 a RIDEM Hearing Officer determined that Power Test is responsible for the discharge of the petroleum product under the Rhode Island Oil Pollution Control Act, R.I.G.L. Section 46-12.5.1-3 and Rule 6(a) and 12(b) of the Oil Pollution Control Regulations.
202947_14_ITEM1_P30_S1	The RIDEM Decision and Order requires Power Test to remediate the contamination as directed by RIDEM and remanded the proposed penalty to RIDEM for recalculation.
202947_14_ITEM1_P30_S2	In November 2008, Power Test appealed the decision to the Rhode Island Superior Court.
202947_14_ITEM1_P30_S3	In addition, in November 2008, Power Test sought, and received, a stay of the Decision and Order of the Hearing Officer pending a clarification by RIDEM of the amount of the proposed penalty.
202947_14_ITEM1_P30_S4	In October 2009, RIDEM issued a recalculated administrative penalty, and, subsequently, the RIDEM Hearing Officer issued a recommended amended decision, which was affirmed as a final decision by the RIDEM Director in December 2009.
202947_14_ITEM1_P30_S5	In January 2010, Power Test appealed that decision to Superior Court.
202947_14_ITEM1_P30_S6	In September 2011, the Superior Court affirmed the decision of the RIDEM director.
202947_14_ITEM1_P30_S7	Power Test has appealed that decision to the Rhode Island Supreme Court.
202947_14_ITEM1_P31_S0	In April 2009, the Company sued Power Test and Getty Properties Corp. in the Rhode Island Superior Court seeking remediation of the site or, in the alternative, the cost of the remediation.
202947_14_ITEM1_P31_S1	On May 1, 2009, Power Test and Getty Properties Corp. removed the action to the United States District Court for the District of Rhode Island ( the Court ).
202947_14_ITEM1_P32_S0	On May 22, 2009, Power Test and Getty Properties Corp. answered the Complaint and filed a Counterclaim against Dunellen, LLC and Capital Terminal Company alleging that Dunellen, LLC and Capital Terminal Company are responsible for the contamination.
202947_14_ITEM1_P32_S1	Getty Properties Corp. and Power Test joined Getty Petroleum Marketing, Inc., the tenant under a long-term lease with Getty Properties Corp. of the adjacent property, as a defendant.
202947_14_ITEM1_P32_S2	The Company amended its Complaint to add Getty Petroleum Marketing, Inc. as a defendant.
202947_14_ITEM1_P32_S3	Getty Petroleum Marketing, Inc. moved for summary judgment against the Company, Getty Properties Corp. and Power Test.
202947_14_ITEM1_P33_S0	On December 5, 2011, Getty Petroleum Marketing, Inc. filed for bankruptcy under Chapter 11 of the United States Bankruptcy Act.
202947_14_ITEM1_P33_S1	Thereafter, with Bankruptcy Court approval, Getty Petroleum Marketing, Inc. rejected its lease with Getty Properties Corp.
202947_14_ITEM1_P33_S2	On August 24, 2012, the Bankruptcy Court approved a plan to liquidate Getty Petroleum Marketing, Inc.
202947_14_ITEM1_P33_S3	On January 15, 2013, the Court granted Getty Petroleum Marketing, Inc. s motion for summary judgment against the Company, Getty Properties Corp. and Power Test, dismissing the Company s third-party complaint.
202947_14_ITEM1_P33_S4	The parties have agreed to stay the litigation pending a determination by the Rhode Island Supreme Court on the Power Test appeal.
202947_14_ITEM1_P33_S5	There can be no assurance that the Company will prevail in this litigation.
202947_14_ITEM1_P33_S6	Since January 2003, the Company has not incurred significant costs in connection with this matter, other than ongoing litigation costs, and is unable to determine the costs it might incur to remedy the situation, as well as any costs to investigate, defend and seek reimbursement from the responsible party with respect to this contamination.
202947_14_ITEM1_P34_S0	In 1994, a leak was discovered in a 25,000 barrel storage tank at the Terminal which allowed the escape of a small amount of fuel oil.
202947_14_ITEM1_P34_S1	All required notices were made to RIDEM.
202947_14_ITEM1_P34_S2	In 2000, the tank was demolished and testing of the groundwater indicated that there was no large pooling of contaminants.
202947_14_ITEM1_P35_S0	In 2001, RIDEM approved a plan pursuant to which the Company installed a passive system consisting of three wells and commenced monitoring the wells.
202947_14_ITEM1_P35_S1	In 2003, RIDEM decided that the passive monitoring system previously approved was not sufficient and required the Company to design an active remediation system for the removal of product from the contaminated site.
202947_14_ITEM1_P36_S0	The consulting engineers estimated a total cost of $200,000 to design, install and operate the system, which amount was accrued in 2004.
202947_14_ITEM1_P36_S1	Through 2006, the Company had expended $119,000 and has not incurred any additional costs since then.
202947_14_ITEM1_P36_S2	In 2011, RIDEM notified the Company to proceed with the next phase of the approval process, notifying the abutters of the proposed remediation system even though RIDEM has not yet taken any action on the Company s proposed plan.
202947_14_ITEM1_P37_S0	As designed, the system will pump out the contaminants which will be disposed of in compliance with applicable regulations.
202947_14_ITEM1_P37_S1	After a period of time, the groundwater will be tested to determine if sufficient contaminants have been removed.
202947_14_ITEM1_P37_S2	While the Company and its consulting engineers believe that the proposed active remediation system will correct the situation, it is possible that RIDEM could require the Company to expand remediation efforts, which could result in the Company incurring costs in excess of the remaining accrual of $81,000.
202947_14_ITEM1_P38_S0	The Company manages its exposure to contamination, remediation or similar costs associated with the Facility through adherence to established procedures for operations and equipment maintenance.
202947_14_ITEM1_P39_S0	Insurance The Company maintains what management believes to be adequate levels of insurance, including environmental insurance.
