202947_15_ITEM8_P6_S0	Description of business: Capital Properties, Inc. and its wholly-owned subsidiaries, Tri-State Displays, Inc., Capital Terminal Company and Dunellen, LLC (collectively referred to as the Company ) operate in two segments, leasing and petroleum storage.
202947_15_ITEM8_P7_S0	The leasing segment consists of the long-term leasing of certain of its real estate interests in downtown Providence, Rhode Island (upon the commencement of which the tenants are required to construct buildings thereon, with the exception of the parking garage and Parcels 6B and 6C), the leasing of a portion of its building ( Steeple Street Building ) under short-term leasing arrangements and the leasing of locations along interstate and primary highways in Rhode Island and Massachusetts to Lamar Outdoor Advertising, LLC ( Lamar ) which has constructed outdoor advertising boards thereon.
202947_15_ITEM8_P7_S1	The Company anticipates that the future development of its remaining properties in and adjacent to the Capital Center area will consist primarily of long-term ground leases.
202947_15_ITEM8_P7_S2	Pending this development, the Company leases these parcels for public parking under short-term leasing arrangements to Metropark, Ltd. ( Metropark ).
202947_15_ITEM8_P8_S0	The petroleum storage segment consists of the petroleum storage terminal (the Terminal ) containing 1,004,000 shell barrels and the Wilkesbarre Pier (the Pier ), both of which are owned by the Company and are collectively referred to as the Facility, located in East Providence, Rhode Island.
202947_15_ITEM8_P8_S1	For the first four months of 2013, the Company operated the Facility for Global Companies, LLC ( Global ) under a lease which expired April 30, 2013.
202947_15_ITEM8_P8_S2	Effective September 1, 2013, the Company entered into a throughput lease with Atlantic Trading Marketing, Inc. ( ATMI ) for 425,000 shell barrels for a term of eight months with automatic three-month extensions unless terminated by either party.
202947_15_ITEM8_P8_S3	In addition, the Company granted ATMI a month-to-month option to lease up to 220,000 additional barrels on an as-used basis.
202947_15_ITEM8_P8_S4	ATMI vacated the Facility on April 30, 2014.
202947_15_ITEM8_P9_S0	Effective May 1, 2014, the Company entered into a Petroleum Storage Services Agreement (the Agreement ) with Sprague Operating Resources, LLC ( Sprague ) for the lease of its entire storage capacity of 1,004,000 barrels for a term of five years.
202947_15_ITEM8_P9_S1	The base rent is $3,500,000, subject to annual cost-of-living adjustments on May 1 of each year.
202947_15_ITEM8_P9_S2	In addition, the Company will receive an additional $.15 for each barrel of throughput at the Facility in excess of 3,500,000 barrels in any contract year (May 1 to April 30).
202947_15_ITEM8_P9_S3	Sprague has the right to extend the Agreement for two additional terms of five years each, provided that Sprague gives at least twelve months notice prior to the expiration of the initial or the extension term, as applicable.
202947_15_ITEM8_P9_S4	Commencing April 1, 2016 and on each April 1 thereafter during the initial term and any extension term, either party during the following thirty days has the right to terminate the Agreement as of April 30 of the year next following the year in which notice of termination is given.
202947_15_ITEM8_P10_S0	Commencing May 1, 2015, Sprague will reimburse the Company for any real property taxes in excess of $290,000.
202947_15_ITEM8_P10_S1	The Agreement contains other customary terms and conditions.
202947_15_ITEM8_P11_S0	The principal difference between the two segments relates to the nature of the operations.
202947_15_ITEM8_P12_S0	In the leasing segment, the tenants under long-term land leases incur substantially all of the development and operating costs of the assets constructed on the Company s land, including the payment of real property taxes on both the land and any improvements constructed thereon.
202947_15_ITEM8_P12_S1	In the petroleum storage segment, the Company is responsible for the operating and maintenance expenditures, as well as capital improvements at the Facility.
202947_15_ITEM8_P13_S0	Summary of significant accounting policies: Principles of consolidation: The accompanying consolidated financial statements include the accounts and transactions of the Company and its wholly-owned subsidiaries.
202947_15_ITEM8_P13_S1	All significant intercompany accounts and transactions have been eliminated in consolidation.
202947_15_ITEM8_P14_S0	Use of estimates: The preparation of consolidated financial statements in conformity with United States generally accepted accounting principles ( GAAP ) requires management to make estimates and assumptions that affect the reported amounts of assets and liabilities and disclosure of contingent assets and liabilities at the date of the financial statements.
202947_15_ITEM8_P14_S1	Estimates also affect the reported amounts of income and expenses during the reporting period.
202947_15_ITEM8_P14_S2	Actual results could differ from those estimates.
202947_15_ITEM8_P15_S0	Fair value of financial instruments: The Company believes that the fair values of its financial instruments, including cash, receivables and payables, approximate their respective book values because of their short-term nature.
202947_15_ITEM8_P15_S1	The fair value of the bank note payable approximates its book value and was determined using borrowing rates currently available to the Company for loans with similar terms and maturities.
202947_15_ITEM8_P15_S2	Based upon an opinion obtained by the Company from an investment banking firm, the fair value of the dividend notes payable approximates their book value.
202947_15_ITEM8_P15_S3	The fair values described herein were determined using significant other observable inputs (Level 2) as defined by GAAP.
202947_15_ITEM8_P16_S0	Properties and equipment: Properties and equipment are stated at cost.
202947_15_ITEM8_P16_S1	Acquisitions and additions are capitalized while routine maintenance and repairs, which do not improve the asset or extend its life, are charged to expense when incurred.
202947_15_ITEM8_P16_S2	Depreciation is being provided by the straight-line method over the estimated useful lives of the respective assets.
202947_15_ITEM8_P17_S0	The Company follows GAAP when accounting for the impairment or disposal of long-lived assets, which requires that properties and equipment held and used by the Company be reviewed for impairment whenever events or changes in circumstances indicate that the net book value of the asset may not be recoverable.
202947_15_ITEM8_P17_S1	An impairment loss will be recognized if the sum of the expected future cash flows (undiscounted and before interest) from the use of the asset is less than the net book value of the asset.
202947_15_ITEM8_P17_S2	Generally, the amount of the impairment loss is measured as the difference between the net book value and the estimated fair value of the asset.
202947_15_ITEM8_P18_S0	Cash and cash equivalents: The Company considers all highly liquid investments with a maturity of three months or less when purchased to be cash equivalents.
202947_15_ITEM8_P18_S1	At December 31, 2014 and 2013, the Company had no cash equivalents.
202947_15_ITEM8_P18_S2	The Company had maintained all of its cash in non-interest bearing checking accounts in one bank which were fully insured by the Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation ( FDIC ).
202947_15_ITEM8_P18_S3	Effective January 1, 2013, the FDIC reduced the insurance on all bank accounts to a maximum of $250,000.
202947_15_ITEM8_P18_S4	The Company has not experienced any losses in such accounts.
202947_15_ITEM8_P19_S0	Initial direct agreement costs: Initial direct agreement costs associated with the execution of a rental agreement are capitalized and amortized on a straight-line basis over the non-cancellable portion of the agreement term.
202947_15_ITEM8_P20_S0	Environmental incidents: The Company accrues a liability when an environmental incident has occurred and the costs are estimable.
202947_15_ITEM8_P20_S1	The Company does not record a receivable for recoveries from third parties for environmental matters until it has determined that the amount of the collection is reasonably assured.
202947_15_ITEM8_P20_S2	The accrued liability is relieved when the Company pays the liability or a third party assumes the liability.
202947_15_ITEM8_P20_S3	Upon determination that collection is reasonably assured or a third party assumes the liability, the Company records the amount as a reduction of expense.
202947_15_ITEM8_P21_S0	The Company charges to expense those costs that do not extend the life, increase the capacity or improve the safety or efficiency of the property owned or used by the Company.
202947_15_ITEM8_P22_S0	Revenues: Leasing The Company s properties leased to others are under operating leases.
202947_15_ITEM8_P22_S1	The Company reports leasing revenue when earned under the operating method.
202947_15_ITEM8_P22_S2	Certain of the Company s long-term land leases, including the outdoor advertising locations, provide for presently known scheduled rent increases over the remaining terms (31 to 139 years).
202947_15_ITEM8_P22_S3	The Company follows GAAP in accounting for leases by recognizing leasing revenue on the straight-line basis over the terms of the leases; however, the Company does not report as revenue that portion of such straight-line rentals which management is unable to conclude is realizable (collectible) due to the length of the lease terms and other related uncertainties.
202947_15_ITEM8_P23_S0	Petroleum storage facility The Company reports revenue from the operations of the Facility when earned and reports as revenue the tenant s portion of the real property taxes and certain other items as required by the lease.
202947_15_ITEM8_P23_S1	Contingent The Company reports contingent revenue in the period in which the factors occur on which the contingent payments are predicated.
202947_15_ITEM8_P24_S0	Income taxes: The Company and its subsidiaries file consolidated income tax returns.
202947_15_ITEM8_P24_S1	The Company provides for income taxes based on income reported for financial reporting purposes.
202947_15_ITEM8_P24_S2	The provision for income taxes differs from the amounts currently payable because of temporary differences associated with the recognition of certain income and expense items for financial reporting and tax reporting purposes.
202947_15_ITEM8_P24_S3	The Company follows GAAP in accounting for uncertainty in income taxes.
202947_15_ITEM8_P24_S4	Based on its evaluation, the Company has concluded that there are no significant uncertain tax positions requiring recognition in the consolidated financial statements.
202947_15_ITEM8_P24_S5	The Company will report any tax-related interest and penalties related to uncertain tax positions as a component of income tax expense.
202947_15_ITEM8_P25_S0	Legal fees: The Company recognizes legal fees as incurred.
202947_15_ITEM8_P26_S0	Basic earnings per common share: Basic earnings per common share are computed by dividing net income by the weighted average number of common shares outstanding during the period.
202947_15_ITEM8_P27_S0	New accounting standards: The Company reviews new accounting standards as issued.
202947_15_ITEM8_P27_S1	Although some of these accounting standards may be applicable to the Company, the Company expects that none of the new standards will have a significant impact on its consolidated financial statements.

202947_15_ITEM8_P34_S4	Net Proceeds is defined as the gross cash received by the Company from any such sale reduced by the sum of (a) costs relating to the sale, (b) federal and state income taxes as a result of the sale, and (c) the amount used by the Company to pay in whole or in part financial institution debts secured by a mortgage of the Company s or any subsidiary s real property regardless of whether such mortgage encumbers the property sold.
202947_15_ITEM8_P34_S5	The Company has obligated itself not to grant any mortgages on any of its property located in the Capital Center District in Providence, Rhode Island, other than Parcels 3S and 5, and to cause its subsidiaries not to grant any such mortgages, in each case without the consent of the holders of two-thirds of the outstanding principal face amount of the Dividend Notes.

202947_15_ITEM8_P44_S3	Sprague has the right to extend the Agreement for two additional terms of five years each, provided that Sprague gives at least twelve months notice prior to the expiration of the initial or the extension term, as applicable.
202947_15_ITEM8_P44_S4	Commencing April 1, 2016 and on each April 1 thereafter during the initial term and any extension term, either party during the following thirty days has the right to terminate the Agreement as of April 30 of the year next following the year in which notice of termination is given.
202947_15_ITEM8_P45_S0	For the year ended December 31, 2014, the Company was not reimbursed for any real property taxes.
202947_15_ITEM8_P45_S1	Commencing May 1, 2015, Sprague will reimburse the Company for any real property taxes in excess of $290,000.
202947_15_ITEM8_P45_S2	The Agreement contains other customary terms and conditions.
202947_15_ITEM8_P46_S0	The Company incurred $108,000 in fees in connection with the execution of the Agreement, which amounts are being amortized on the straight-line method over the three-year non-cancellable portion of the term of the Agreement and are included in petroleum storage facility expenses on the accompanying consolidated statement of income for the year ended December 31, 2014.
202947_15_ITEM8_P46_S1	At December 31, 2014, deferred agreement costs are $84,000, which is included in prepaid and other on the accompanying consolidated balance sheet as of December 31, 2014.
202947_15_ITEM8_P47_S0	The Pier is a deep-water pier in East Providence, Rhode Island owned by the Company which is integral to the operation of the Terminal.
202947_15_ITEM8_P47_S1	The Pier and the Terminal are connected by two petroleum pipelines which the Company has a permanent right to use.
202947_15_ITEM8_P48_S0	Environmental incident (2002): In 2002, during testing of monitoring wells at the Terminal, the Company s consulting engineer discovered free floating phase product in a groundwater monitoring well located on that portion of the Terminal purchased in 2000.
202947_15_ITEM8_P48_S1	Laboratory analysis indicated that the product was gasoline, which is not a product the Company ever stored at the Terminal.
202947_15_ITEM8_P48_S2	The Company commenced an environmental investigation and analysis, the results of which indicate that the gasoline did not come from the Terminal.
202947_15_ITEM8_P48_S3	The Company notified the Rhode Island Department of Environmental Management ( RIDEM ).
202947_15_ITEM8_P48_S4	RIDEM subsequently identified Power Test Realty Partnership ( Power Test ), the owner of an adjacent parcel, as a potentially responsible party for the contamination.
202947_15_ITEM8_P48_S5	Getty Properties Corp. is the general partner of Power Test.
202947_15_ITEM8_P49_S0	Power Test challenged that determination and, after an administrative hearing, in October 2008 a RIDEM Hearing Officer determined that Power Test is responsible for the discharge of the petroleum product under the Rhode Island Oil Pollution Control Act, R.I.G.L. Section 46-12.5.1-3 and Rule 6(a) and 12(b) of the Oil Pollution Control Regulations.
202947_15_ITEM8_P49_S1	The RIDEM Decision and Order requires Power Test to remediate the contamination as directed by RIDEM and remanded the proposed penalty to RIDEM for recalculation.
202947_15_ITEM8_P49_S2	In November 2008, Power Test appealed the decision to the Rhode Island Superior Court.
202947_15_ITEM8_P49_S3	In addition, in November 2008, Power Test sought, and received, a stay of the Decision and Order of the Hearing Officer pending a clarification by RIDEM of the amount of the proposed penalty.
202947_15_ITEM8_P49_S4	In October 2009, RIDEM issued a recalculated administrative penalty, and, subsequently, the RIDEM Hearing Officer issued a recommended amended decision, which was affirmed as a final decision by the RIDEM Director in December 2009.
202947_15_ITEM8_P49_S5	In January 2010, Power Test appealed that decision to the Superior Court.
202947_15_ITEM8_P49_S6	In September 2011, the Superior Court affirmed the decision of the RIDEM director.
202947_15_ITEM8_P49_S7	Power Test has appealed that decision to the Rhode Island Supreme Court.
202947_15_ITEM8_P49_S8	The Supreme Court has not decided the appeal.
202947_15_ITEM8_P50_S0	In April 2009, the Company sued Power Test and Getty Properties Corp. in the Rhode Island Superior Court seeking remediation of the site or, in the alternative, the cost of the remediation.
202947_15_ITEM8_P50_S1	On May 1, 2009, Power Test and Getty Properties Corp. removed the action to the United States District Court for the District of Rhode Island ( the Court ).
202947_15_ITEM8_P51_S0	On May 22, 2009, Power Test and Getty Properties Corp. answered the Complaint and filed a Counterclaim against Dunellen, LLC and Capital Terminal Company alleging that Dunellen, LLC and Capital Terminal Company are responsible for the contamination.
202947_15_ITEM8_P51_S1	Getty Properties Corp. and Power Test joined Getty Petroleum Marketing, Inc., the tenant under a long-term lease with Getty Properties Corp. of the adjacent property, as a defendant.
202947_15_ITEM8_P51_S2	The Company amended its Complaint to add Getty Petroleum Marketing, Inc. as a defendant.
202947_15_ITEM8_P51_S3	Getty Petroleum Marketing, Inc. moved for summary judgment against the Company, Getty Properties Corp. and Power Test.
202947_15_ITEM8_P52_S0	On December 5, 2011, Getty Petroleum Marketing, Inc. filed for bankruptcy under Chapter 11 of the United States Bankruptcy Act.
202947_15_ITEM8_P52_S1	Thereafter, with Bankruptcy Court approval, Getty Petroleum Marketing, Inc. rejected its lease with Getty Properties Corp.
202947_15_ITEM8_P52_S2	On August 24, 2012, the Bankruptcy Court approved a plan to liquidate Getty Petroleum Marketing, Inc.
202947_15_ITEM8_P52_S3	On January 15, 2013, the Court granted Getty Petroleum Marketing, Inc. s motion for summary judgment against the Company, Getty Properties Corp. and Power Test, dismissing the Company s third-party complaint.
202947_15_ITEM8_P52_S4	The parties have agreed to stay the litigation pending a determination by the Rhode Island Supreme Court on the Power Test appeal.
202947_15_ITEM8_P52_S5	There can be no assurance that the Company will prevail in this litigation.
202947_15_ITEM8_P52_S6	Since January 2003, the Company has not incurred significant costs in connection with this matter, other than ongoing litigation costs, and is unable to determine the costs it might incur to remedy the situation, as well as any costs to investigate, defend and seek reimbursement from the responsible party with respect to this contamination.
202947_15_ITEM8_P53_S0	In 1994, a leak was discovered in a 25,000 barrel storage tank at the Terminal which allowed the escape of a small amount of fuel oil.
202947_15_ITEM8_P53_S1	All required notices were made to RIDEM.
202947_15_ITEM8_P53_S2	In 2000, the tank was demolished and testing of the groundwater indicated that there was no large pooling of contaminants.
202947_15_ITEM8_P54_S0	In 2001, RIDEM approved a plan pursuant to which the Company installed a passive system consisting of three wells and commenced monitoring the wells.
202947_15_ITEM8_P55_S0	In 2003, RIDEM decided that the passive monitoring system previously approved was not sufficient and required the Company to design an active remediation system for the removal of product from the contaminated site.
202947_15_ITEM8_P55_S1	The Company and its consulting engineers began the pre-design testing of the site in the fourth quarter of 2004.
202947_15_ITEM8_P55_S2	The consulting engineers estimated a total cost of $200,000 to design, install and operate the system, which amount was accrued in 2004.
202947_15_ITEM8_P55_S3	Through 2006, the Company had expended $119,000 and has not incurred any significant costs since then.
202947_15_ITEM8_P55_S4	In 2011, RIDEM notified the company to proceed with the next phase of the approval process, notifying the abutters of the proposed remediation system even though RIDEM has not yet taken any action on the Company s proposed plan.
202947_15_ITEM8_P56_S0	As designed, the system will pump out the contaminants which will be disposed of in compliance with applicable regulations.
202947_15_ITEM8_P56_S1	After a period of time, the groundwater will be tested to determine if sufficient contaminants have been removed.
202947_15_ITEM8_P56_S2	In 2014, the Company engaged new consultants to work with RIDEM to develop the next phase of the approval process.
202947_15_ITEM8_P56_S3	While the Company and its consulting engineers believe that the proposed active remediation system will correct the situation, it is possible that RIDEM could require the Company to expand remediation efforts, which could result in the Company incurring costs in excess of the remaining accrual of $80,000.

202947_16_ITEM1_P0_S0	Development The Company was organized as a business corporation under the laws of Rhode Island in 1983 as Providence and Worcester Company and is the successor by merger in 1983 to a corporation also named Providence and Worcester Company which was organized under the laws of Delaware in 1979.
202947_16_ITEM1_P0_S1	In 1984, the Company s name was changed to Capital Properties, Inc.
202947_16_ITEM1_P1_S0	Segments The Company operates in two segments: leasing and petroleum storage.
202947_16_ITEM1_P1_S1	For financial information, see Note 9 of Notes to Consolidated Financial Statements in Item 8.
202947_16_ITEM1_P2_S0	The leasing segment is principally devoted to the leasing of Company-owned land in the Capital Center area ( Capital Center ) in downtown Providence, Rhode Island under long-term ground leases.
202947_16_ITEM1_P2_S1	The Company owns approximately 18 acres in the Capital Center consisting of 13 individual parcels.
202947_16_ITEM1_P3_S0	The Capital Center (approximately 77 acres of land) is the result of a development project undertaken by the State of Rhode Island, the City of Providence, the National Railroad Passenger Corporation ( Amtrak ) and the Company during the 1980 s in which two rivers, the Moshassuck and the Woonasquatucket, were moved, Amtrak s Northeast Corridor rail line was relocated, a new Amtrak/commuter railroad station was constructed and significant public improvements were made to improve pedestrian and vehicular traffic in the area.
202947_16_ITEM1_P3_S1	With the exception of the Steeple Street property, the Company has not acted, and does not intend to act, as a developer with respect to any improvements constructed on Company-owned parcels.
202947_16_ITEM1_P3_S2	Rather, the Company offers individual parcels for lease pursuant to long-term ground leases with terms of 99 years or more.
202947_16_ITEM1_P3_S3	Each lease contains provisions permitting the tenant to develop the parcel under certain terms and conditions.
202947_16_ITEM1_P3_S4	Each lease provides for periodic rent adjustments of various kinds.
202947_16_ITEM1_P4_S0	Under the leases, the tenants are responsible for insuring the Company against various hazards and events.
202947_16_ITEM1_P4_S1	Each tenant is required to indemnify the Company with respect to all of the tenant s activities on the land.
202947_16_ITEM1_P4_S2	The leases contain other terms and conditions customary to such instruments.
202947_16_ITEM1_P5_S0	The Company first began offering parcels for lease in the Capital Center area in the late 1980 s.
202947_16_ITEM1_P5_S1	As of December 31, 2015, nine parcels have been leased by the Company under long-term leases of 99 years or more.

202947_16_ITEM1_P10_S1	All but one of these locations are controlled by the Company through permanent easements granted to the Company pursuant to an agreement between the Company and Providence Worcester Railroad Company, a related company ( Railroad the remaining location is leased by the Company from a third party with a remaining term of four years.
202947_16_ITEM1_P10_S2	Although no new locations have been added since 2002, in 2013 Lamar converted billboards at two locations to electronic boards, which conversions extended the term of the lease for a total of twelve years to 2045.
202947_16_ITEM1_P10_S3	Lamar has a right of first refusal for additional billboard location sites acquired by the Company in New England and Metropolitan New York City.
202947_16_ITEM1_P10_S4	The lease with Lamar provides, among other things, for the following: (1) the base rent increases annually at the rate of 2.75% for each leased billboard location commencing June 1, 2006 and on each June 1 thereafter; and (2) in addition to base rent, for each 12-month period commencing each June 1, Lamar must pay to the Company 30% of the gross revenues from each standard billboard and 20% of the gross revenues from each electronic billboard for such 12-month period, reduced by the sum of (a) commissions paid to third parties and (b) the base monthly rent for each leased billboard display for such 12-month period.

202947_16_ITEM1_P16_S0	Petroleum Storage Terminal and Pier Facility The Company, through its wholly-owned subsidiary, Dunellen, LLC, owns a petroleum storage terminal containing 1,004,000 shell barrels (the Terminal ) and the Wilkesbarre Pier (the Pier ), collectively referred to as the Facility, located in East Providence, Rhode Island.
202947_16_ITEM1_P16_S1	The Terminal utilizes the Pier and pipelines connecting the Pier to the Terminal.
202947_16_ITEM1_P16_S2	Leasing of the Facility For the first four months of 2014, the Company leased a portion of the Facility (425,000 shell barrels) to Atlantic Trading Marketing, Inc. which vacated the Facility on April 30, 2014.
202947_16_ITEM1_P16_S3	On May 1, 2014, the Company entered into a Petroleum Storage Services Agreement (the Agreement ) with Sprague Operating Resources, LLC ( Sprague ) for the lease of its entire storage capacity of 1,004,000 barrels for a term of five years.
202947_16_ITEM1_P16_S4	The base rent is $3,500,000, subject to annual cost-of-living adjustments on May 1 of each year.
202947_16_ITEM1_P16_S5	In addition, the Company will receive an additional $.15 for each barrel of throughput at the Facility in excess of 3,500,000 barrels in any contract year (May 1 to April 30).
202947_16_ITEM1_P16_S6	Sprague has the right to extend the Agreement for two additional terms of five years each, provided that Sprague gives at least twelve months notice prior to the expiration of the initial or the extension term, as applicable.
202947_16_ITEM1_P16_S7	Commencing April 1, 2016 and on each April 1 thereafter during the initial term and any extension term, either party during the following thirty days has the right to terminate the Agreement as of April 30 of the year next following the year in which notice of termination is given.
202947_16_ITEM1_P17_S0	Commencing May 1, 2015, Sprague will reimburse the Company for any real property taxes in excess of $290,000.
202947_16_ITEM1_P17_S1	The Agreement contains other customary terms and conditions.
202947_16_ITEM1_P18_S0	The operation of a petroleum storage facility carries with it the risk of environmental contamination.
202947_16_ITEM1_P19_S0	In 2002, during testing of monitoring wells at the Terminal, the Company s consulting engineer discovered free floating phase product in a groundwater monitoring well located on that portion of the Terminal purchased in 2000.
202947_16_ITEM1_P19_S1	Laboratory analysis indicated that the product was gasoline, which is not a product the Company ever stored at the Terminal.
202947_16_ITEM1_P19_S2	The Company commenced an environmental investigation and analysis, the results of which indicate that the gasoline did not come from the Terminal.
202947_16_ITEM1_P19_S3	The Company notified the Rhode Island Department of Environmental Management ( RIDEM ).
202947_16_ITEM1_P19_S4	RIDEM subsequently identified Power Test Realty Partnership ( Power Test ), the owner of an adjacent parcel, as a potentially responsible party for the contamination.
202947_16_ITEM1_P19_S5	Getty Properties Corp. is the general partner of Power Test.
202947_16_ITEM1_P20_S0	Power Test challenged that determination and, after an administrative hearing, in October 2008 a RIDEM Hearing Officer determined that Power Test is responsible for the discharge of the petroleum product under the Rhode Island Oil Pollution Control Act, R.I.G.L. Section 46-12.5.1-3 and Rule 6(a) and 12(b) of the Oil Pollution Control Regulations.
202947_16_ITEM1_P20_S1	The RIDEM Decision and Order requires Power Test to remediate the contamination as directed by RIDEM and remanded the proposed penalty to RIDEM for recalculation.
202947_16_ITEM1_P20_S2	In November 2008, Power Test appealed the decision to the Rhode Island Superior Court.
202947_16_ITEM1_P20_S3	In addition, in November 2008, Power Test sought, and received, a stay of the Decision and Order of the Hearing Officer pending a clarification by RIDEM of the amount of the proposed penalty.
202947_16_ITEM1_P20_S4	In October 2009, RIDEM issued a recalculated administrative penalty, and, subsequently, the RIDEM Hearing Officer issued a recommended amended decision, which was affirmed as a final decision by the RIDEM Director in December 2009.
202947_16_ITEM1_P20_S5	In January 2010, Power Test appealed that decision to Superior Court.
202947_16_ITEM1_P20_S6	In September 2011, the Superior Court affirmed the decision of the RIDEM director.
202947_16_ITEM1_P20_S7	Power Test has appealed that decision to the Rhode Island Supreme Court.
202947_16_ITEM1_P20_S8	On March 4, 2016 the Supreme Court affirmed the decision of the Superior Court and the 2009 decision of the RIDEM Director.
202947_16_ITEM1_P21_S0	In April 2009, the Company sued Power Test and Getty Properties Corp. in the Rhode Island Superior Court seeking remediation of the site or, in the alternative, the cost of the remediation.
202947_16_ITEM1_P21_S1	On May 1, 2009, Power Test and Getty Properties Corp. removed the action to the United States District Court for the District of Rhode Island ( the Court ).
202947_16_ITEM1_P22_S0	On May 22, 2009, Power Test and Getty Properties Corp. answered the Complaint and filed a Counterclaim against Dunellen, LLC and Capital Terminal Company alleging that Dunellen, LLC and Capital Terminal Company are responsible for the contamination.
202947_16_ITEM1_P22_S1	Getty Properties Corp. and Power Test joined Getty Petroleum Marketing, Inc., the tenant under a long-term lease with Getty Properties Corp. of the adjacent property, as a defendant.
202947_16_ITEM1_P22_S2	The Company amended its Complaint to add Getty Petroleum Marketing, Inc. as a defendant.
202947_16_ITEM1_P23_S0	Marketing, Inc. moved for summary judgment against the Company, Getty Properties Corp. and Power Test.
202947_16_ITEM1_P24_S0	On December 5, 2011, Getty Petroleum Marketing, Inc. filed for bankruptcy under Chapter 11 of the United States Bankruptcy Act.
202947_16_ITEM1_P24_S1	Thereafter, with Bankruptcy Court approval, Getty Petroleum Marketing, Inc. rejected its lease with Getty Properties Corp.
202947_16_ITEM1_P24_S2	On August 24, 2012, the Bankruptcy Court approved a plan to liquidate Getty Petroleum Marketing, Inc.
202947_16_ITEM1_P24_S3	On January 15, 2013, the Court granted Getty Petroleum Marketing, Inc. s motion for summary judgment against the Company, Getty Properties Corp. and Power Test, dismissing the Company s third-party complaint.
202947_16_ITEM1_P24_S4	The parties have agreed to stay the litigation pending a determination by the Rhode Island Supreme Court on the Power Test appeal.
202947_16_ITEM1_P25_S0	The Company is in the process of evaluating its position in the light of the Rhode Island Supreme Court decision referred to above.
202947_16_ITEM1_P25_S1	Since January 2003, the Company has not incurred significant costs in connection with this matter, other than ongoing litigation costs, and is unable to determine the costs it might incur to remedy the situation, as well as any costs to investigate, defend and seek reimbursement from the responsible party with respect to this contamination.
202947_16_ITEM1_P26_S0	In 1994, a leak was discovered in a 25,000 barrel storage tank at the Terminal which allowed the escape of a small amount of fuel oil.
202947_16_ITEM1_P26_S1	All required notices were made to RIDEM.
202947_16_ITEM1_P26_S2	In 2000, the tank was demolished and testing of the groundwater indicated that there was no large pooling of contaminants.
202947_16_ITEM1_P27_S0	In 2001, RIDEM approved a plan pursuant to which the Company installed a passive system consisting of three wells and commenced monitoring the wells.
202947_16_ITEM1_P27_S1	In 2003, RIDEM decided that the passive monitoring system previously approved was not sufficient and required the Company to design an active remediation system for the removal of product from the contaminated site.
202947_16_ITEM1_P27_S2	The Company and its consulting engineers began the pre-design testing of the site in the fourth quarter of 2004.
202947_16_ITEM1_P27_S3	The consulting engineers estimated a total cost of $200,000 to design, install and operate the system, which amount was accrued in 2004.
202947_16_ITEM1_P27_S4	Through 2006, the Company had expended $119,000 and has not incurred any significant costs since then.
202947_16_ITEM1_P27_S5	In 2011, RIDEM notified the Company to proceed with the next phase of the approval process, notifying the abutters of the proposed remediation system even though RIDEM has not yet taken any action on the Company s proposed plan.
202947_16_ITEM1_P28_S0	As designed, the system will pump out the contaminants which will be disposed of in compliance with applicable regulations.
202947_16_ITEM1_P28_S1	After a period of time, the groundwater will be tested to determine if sufficient contaminants have been removed.
202947_16_ITEM1_P28_S2	In 2014, the Company engaged new consultants to work with RIDEM to develop the next phase of the approval process.
202947_16_ITEM1_P28_S3	While the Company and its consulting engineers believe that the proposed active remediation system will correct the situation, it is possible that RIDEM could require the Company to expand remediation efforts, which could result in the Company incurring costs in excess of the remaining accrual of $79,000.
202947_16_ITEM1_P29_S0	The Company manages its exposure to contamination, remediation or similar costs associated with the Facility through adherence to established procedures for operations and equipment maintenance.
202947_16_ITEM1_P30_S0	Insurance The Company maintains what management believes to be adequate levels of insurance, including environmental insurance.
202947_16_ITEM1_P31_S0	Competition The Facility competes with several other similar facilities located on and adjacent to the Providence Harbor.
202947_16_ITEM1_P32_S0	The Terminal has approximately 48% of the total distillate storage capacity in the Providence area.
202947_16_ITEM1_P32_S1	The current tenant, Sprague, competes with other terminal operators on the basis of price, availability and a willingness to advance credit to local wholesalers.
202947_16_ITEM1_P32_S2	The amount of petroleum throughput at the Terminal is a function of Sprague s ability to compete effectively in the marketplace and the amount of product Sprague sells at its City of Providence terminal.
202947_16_ITEM1_P32_S3	The Terminal employs eight people on a full-time basis.

202947_16_ITEM7_P0_S0	Critical accounting policies: The Securities and Exchange Commission ( SEC ) has issued guidance for the disclosure of critical accounting policies.
202947_16_ITEM7_P0_S1	The SEC defines such policies as those that require application of management s most difficult, subjective or complex judgments, often as a result of the need to make estimates about the effect of matters that are inherently uncertain and may change in subsequent periods.
202947_16_ITEM7_P0_S2	The Company s significant accounting policies are described in Note 2 of Notes to Consolidated Financial Statements in Item 8.
202947_16_ITEM7_P0_S3	Not all of these significant accounting policies require management to make difficult, subjective or complex judgments or estimates.
202947_16_ITEM7_P0_S4	Management believes that the Company s revenue recognition policy for long-term leases with scheduled rent increases (leasing segment) meets the SEC definition of critical.
202947_16_ITEM7_P0_S5	Certain of the Company s long-term land leases have original terms of 30 to 149 years and contain scheduled rent increases where the future dollar increases are known at the time of the commencement of the lease or at a subsequent date.
202947_16_ITEM7_P0_S6	The first such lease commenced in 1988, had an original term of 99 years and provides for fixed percentage increases at specified intervals (as well as reappraisal increases).
202947_16_ITEM7_P1_S0	In accordance with United States generally accepted accounting principles ( GAAP ) in accounting for leases, rental income related to the fixed percentage increases that are presently known should be recognized on a straight-line basis.
202947_16_ITEM7_P1_S1	To calculate the annual straight-line amount, the 99 known annual rental amounts are totaled and this total is divided by 99.
202947_16_ITEM7_P1_S2	In 2009, a scheduled appraisal occurred, resulting in a rental increase.
202947_16_ITEM7_P1_S3	The Company recalculated the future annual straight-line amount using the remaining years under the lease.
202947_16_ITEM7_P1_S4	The turnaround date discussed below did not change.
202947_16_ITEM7_P2_S0	For this lease, the calculated annual straight-line amount for 1988 was eight times (multiple) the amount paid by the tenant under the terms of the lease (the contractual amount ).
202947_16_ITEM7_P2_S1	In subsequent years, as the tenant pays higher rents, the multiple gradually decreases until the 57 th year of the lease, at which time the contractual amount paid by the tenant will exceed the calculated straight-line amount.
202947_16_ITEM7_P2_S2	If the Company were to report annual revenue for this lease using the straight-line amount, it would record a significant receivable for each of the first 56 years, which receivable would grow to approximately $34,000,000.
202947_16_ITEM7_P2_S3	Management does not believe that the Company should record a receivable that would not begin to be collected until the 56 th year (the turnaround date ) since management could not be assured of collection.
202947_16_ITEM7_P2_S4	In 1988, management met with the SEC accounting staff to discuss its concerns in applying GAAP as it related to a lease of this length which results in the recording of such a significant receivable that would remain on the Company s balance sheet and continue to grow on an annual basis with a turnaround date so far in the future.
202947_16_ITEM7_P2_S5	The Company presented the SEC accounting staff with an application of the accounting policy whereby management would evaluate the collectibility of the receivable on an annual basis and report as leasing revenue only that portion of the receivable that management could presently conclude would be collectible.
202947_16_ITEM7_P2_S6	The SEC accounting staff did not object to this application by the Company.
202947_16_ITEM7_P2_S7	Through December 31, 2015, the receivable on this lease has grown to $22,716,000 (cumulative excess of straight-line over contractual rentals) and management has not been able to conclude that any portion is collectible as the turnaround date is still 30 years away.
202947_16_ITEM7_P3_S0	In 2004, a second such lease commenced with an original term of 149 years and provides for fixed minimum percentage increases at specified intervals (as well as reappraisal increases).
202947_16_ITEM7_P3_S1	For this lease, the contractual amount paid by the tenant will not exceed the calculated straight-line amount until the 94 th year of the lease.
202947_16_ITEM7_P3_S2	Through December 31, 2015, the receivable on this lease is $26,650,000 (cumulative excess of straight-line over contractual rentals) and management has not been able to conclude that any portion is collectible as the turnaround date is 82 years away.
202947_16_ITEM7_P4_S0	In 2006, the Company entered into an Amended and Restated Agreement of its lease with Lamar Outdoor Advertising LLC ( Lamar ).
202947_16_ITEM7_P4_S1	In 2013, the lease was extended to 2045 following the conversion of billboards at two locations to electronic boards, as required by the lease, resulting in a current remaining term of 30 years which provides for fixed percentage increases annually.
202947_16_ITEM7_P4_S2	For this lease, the contractual amount paid by Lamar will not exceed the calculated straight-line amount until the 23rd year of the extended lease.
202947_16_ITEM7_P4_S3	Through December 31, 2015, the receivable on this lease is $2,190,000 (cumulative excess of straight-line over contractual rentals) and management has not been able to conclude that any portion is collectible as the turnaround date is 14 years away.
202947_16_ITEM7_P5_S0	Accordingly, the Company has not reported any portion of these amounts as leasing revenue in its consolidated financial statements and does not anticipate that it can reach such a conclusion until the turnaround dates are closer.
202947_16_ITEM7_P5_S1	Although the Company s other long-term land leases provide for scheduled rent increases, the provisions of the leases are such that certain future dollar amounts could not be calculated either at the time of the commencement of the lease or now, as such amounts are based on factors that are not presently known, i.e., future cost-of-living adjustments or future appraised values.
202947_16_ITEM7_P5_S2	Through December 31, 2015, the receivable on these leases is $14,389,000 and management has not been able to conclude that any portion is collectible as the turnaround dates are approximately 45 years away.
202947_16_ITEM7_P6_S0	Segments: The Company operates in two segments: leasing and petroleum storage.
202947_16_ITEM7_P6_S1	The leasing segment consists of the long-term leasing of certain of its real estate interests in downtown Providence, Rhode Island (upon the commencement of which the tenants have been required to construct buildings thereon, with the exception of the parking garage and Parcels 6B and 6C), the leasing of a portion of the Steeple Street Building under short-term leasing arrangements and the leasing of locations along interstate and primary highways in Rhode Island and Massachusetts to Lamar which has constructed outdoor advertising boards thereon.
202947_16_ITEM7_P6_S2	The Company anticipates that the future development of its remaining properties in and adjacent to the Capital Center area will consist primarily of long-term ground leases.
202947_16_ITEM7_P6_S3	Pending this development, the Company leases these parcels for public parking under short-term leasing arrangements to Metropark.
202947_16_ITEM7_P7_S0	The petroleum storage segment consists of operating the petroleum storage terminal (the Terminal ) containing 1,004,000 shell barrels and the Wilkesbarre Pier (the Pier ), both of which are owned by the Company and are collectively referred to as the Facility, located in East Providence, Rhode Island for Sprague Operating Resources, LLC ( Sprague ), a wholly-owned subsidiary of Sprague Resources LP, which stores and distributes petroleum products.
202947_16_ITEM7_P7_S1	The principal difference between the two segments relates to the nature of the operations.
202947_16_ITEM7_P8_S0	In the leasing segment, the tenants under long-term land leases incur substantially all of the development and operating costs of the assets constructed on the Company s land, including the payment of real property taxes on both the land and any improvements constructed thereon.
202947_16_ITEM7_P8_S1	In the petroleum storage segment, the Company is responsible for the operating and maintenance expenditures and real estate taxes up to $290,000, as well as capital improvements at the Facility.
202947_16_ITEM7_P9_S0	Liquidity and capital resources: Bank loan: In December 2012, the Company and the Bank entered into an Amended and Restated Loan Agreement pursuant to which the Company refinanced the $2,700,000 balance of the 2010 debt to the Bank and borrowed an additional $3,025,000.
202947_16_ITEM7_P9_S1	In November 2015, the loan was paid in full.
202947_16_ITEM7_P10_S0	Dividend notes: On December 7, 2012, the Board of Directors of the Company declared an extraordinary dividend of $2.25 per share on its Class A and Class B common stock to shareholders of record on December 17, 2012.
202947_16_ITEM7_P10_S1	On December 27, 2012, the Company paid out $3,063,000 in cash and issued $11,787,000 in principal face amount of 5% dividend notes due December 26, 2022 (the Dividend Notes ).
202947_16_ITEM7_P10_S2	The Dividend Notes are unsecured general obligations of the Company bearing interest at the annual rate of 5% payable semi-annually on June 15 and December 15 to note holders of record on June 1 and December 1 of each year.
202947_16_ITEM7_P10_S3	The Dividend Notes may be redeemed in whole or in part at any time and from time to time at the option of the Company.
202947_16_ITEM7_P10_S4	The Dividend Notes are subject to mandatory redemption in an amount equal to the Net Proceeds from the sale of any real property owned by the Company or any of its subsidiaries.
202947_16_ITEM7_P10_S5	Net Proceeds is defined as the gross cash received by the Company from any such sale reduced by the sum of (a) costs relating to the sale, (b) federal and state income taxes as a result of the sale, and (c) the amount used by the Company to pay in whole or in part financial institution debts secured by a mortgage of the Company s or any subsidiary s real property regardless of whether such mortgage encumbers the property sold.
202947_16_ITEM7_P10_S6	The Company has obligated itself not to grant any mortgages on any of its property located in the Capital Center District in Providence, Rhode Island and to cause its subsidiaries not to grant any such mortgages, in each case without the consent of the holders of two-thirds of the outstanding principal face amount of the Dividend Notes.
202947_16_ITEM7_P11_S0	The Dividend Notes contain other customary terms and conditions.
202947_16_ITEM7_P11_S1	The interest payments on an annual basis total $589,000.
202947_16_ITEM7_P12_S0	Petroleum storage facility: For the first four months of 2014, the Company leased a portion of the Facility (425,000 shell barrels) to Atlantic Trading Marketing, Inc. ( ATMI ) which vacated the Facility on April 30, 2014.

202947_16_ITEM8_P0_S4	We conducted our audits in accordance with the standards of the Public Company Accounting Oversight Board (United States).
202947_16_ITEM8_P0_S5	Those standards require that we plan and perform the audit to obtain reasonable assurance about whether the financial statements are free of material misstatement.
202947_16_ITEM8_P0_S6	The Company is not required to have, nor were we engaged to perform, an audit of its internal control over financial reporting.
202947_16_ITEM8_P0_S7	Our audits included consideration of internal control over financial reporting as a basis for designing audit procedures that are appropriate in the circumstances, but not for the purpose of expressing an opinion on the effectiveness of the Company s internal control over financial reporting.
202947_16_ITEM8_P0_S8	Accordingly, we express no such opinion.
202947_16_ITEM8_P1_S0	An audit also includes examining, on a test basis, evidence supporting the amounts and disclosures in the financial statements, assessing the accounting principles used and significant estimates made by management, as well as evaluating the overall financial statement presentation.
202947_16_ITEM8_P1_S1	We believe that our audits provide a reasonable basis for our opinion.

202947_16_ITEM8_P5_S0	Description of business: Capital Properties, Inc. and its wholly-owned subsidiaries, Tri-State Displays, Inc., Capital Terminal Company and Dunellen, LLC (collectively referred to as the Company ) operate in two segments, leasing and petroleum storage.
202947_16_ITEM8_P6_S0	The leasing segment consists of the long-term leasing of certain of its real estate interests in downtown Providence, Rhode Island (upon the commencement of which the tenants are required to construct buildings thereon, with the exception of the parking garage and Parcels 6B and 6C), the leasing of a portion of its building ( Steeple Street Building ) under short-term leasing arrangements and the leasing of locations along interstate and primary highways in Rhode Island and Massachusetts to Lamar Outdoor Advertising, LLC ( Lamar ) which has constructed outdoor advertising boards thereon.
202947_16_ITEM8_P6_S1	The Company anticipates that the future development of its remaining properties in and adjacent to the Capital Center area will consist primarily of long-term ground leases.
202947_16_ITEM8_P6_S2	Pending this development, the Company leases these parcels for public parking under short-term leasing arrangements to Metropark, Ltd. ( Metropark ).
202947_16_ITEM8_P7_S0	The petroleum storage segment consists of operating the petroleum storage terminal (the Terminal ) containing 1,004,000 shell barrels and the Wilkesbarre Pier (the Pier ), both of which are owned by the Company and are collectively referred to as the Facility, located in East Providence, Rhode Island, for Sprague Operating Resources, LLC ( Sprague ), a wholly-owned subsidiary of Sprague Resources, LP, which stores and distributes petroleum products.
202947_16_ITEM8_P7_S1	The principal difference between the two segments relates to the nature of the operations.
202947_16_ITEM8_P8_S0	In the leasing segment, the tenants under long-term land leases incur substantially all of the development and operating costs of the assets constructed on the Company s land, including the payment of real property taxes on both the land and any improvements constructed thereon.
202947_16_ITEM8_P8_S1	In the petroleum storage segment, the Company is responsible for the operating and maintenance expenditures and real estate taxes up to $290,000, as well as capital improvements at the Facility.
202947_16_ITEM8_P9_S0	Summary of significant accounting policies: Principles of consolidation: The accompanying consolidated financial statements include the accounts and transactions of the Company and its wholly-owned subsidiaries.
202947_16_ITEM8_P9_S1	All significant intercompany accounts and transactions have been eliminated in consolidation.
202947_16_ITEM8_P10_S0	Use of estimates: The preparation of consolidated financial statements in conformity with United States generally accepted accounting principles ( GAAP ) requires management to make estimates and assumptions that affect the reported amounts of assets and liabilities and disclosure of contingent assets and liabilities at the date of the financial statements.
202947_16_ITEM8_P10_S1	Estimates also affect the reported amounts of income and expenses during the reporting period.
202947_16_ITEM8_P10_S2	Actual results could differ from those estimates.
202947_16_ITEM8_P11_S0	Fair value of financial instruments: The Company believes that the fair values of its financial instruments, including cash, receivables and payables, approximate their respective book values because of their short-term nature.
202947_16_ITEM8_P11_S1	Upon review of current market conditions and other factors, the Company believes that the fair value of the dividend notes payable approximates their book value.
202947_16_ITEM8_P11_S2	The fair values described herein were determined using significant other observable inputs (Level 2) as defined by GAAP.
202947_16_ITEM8_P12_S0	Properties and equipment: Properties and equipment are stated at cost.
202947_16_ITEM8_P12_S1	Acquisitions and additions are capitalized while routine maintenance and repairs, which do not improve the asset or extend its life, are charged to expense when incurred.
202947_16_ITEM8_P12_S2	Depreciation is being provided by the straight-line method over the estimated useful lives of the respective assets.
202947_16_ITEM8_P13_S0	The Company follows GAAP when accounting for the impairment or disposal of long-lived assets, which requires that properties and equipment held and used by the Company be reviewed for impairment whenever events or changes in circumstances indicate that the net book value of the asset may not be recoverable.
202947_16_ITEM8_P14_S0	will be recognized if the sum of the expected future cash flows (undiscounted and before interest) from the use of the asset is less than the net book value of the asset.
202947_16_ITEM8_P14_S1	Generally, the amount of the impairment loss is measured as the difference between the net book value and the estimated fair value of the asset.
202947_16_ITEM8_P15_S0	Cash and cash equivalents: The Company considers all highly liquid investments with a maturity of three months or less when purchased to be cash equivalents.
202947_16_ITEM8_P15_S1	At December 31, 2015 and 2014, the Company had no cash equivalents.
202947_16_ITEM8_P16_S0	The Company and its three subsidiary companies each maintain a checking account in the same bank, each of which accounts is insured by the Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation to a maximum of $250,000.
202947_16_ITEM8_P16_S1	The Company has not experienced any losses in such accounts.
202947_16_ITEM8_P17_S0	Initial direct agreement costs: Initial direct agreement costs associated with the execution of a rental agreement are capitalized and amortized on a straight-line basis over the non-cancellable portion of the agreement term.
202947_16_ITEM8_P18_S0	Environmental incidents: The Company accrues a liability when an environmental incident has occurred and the costs are estimable.
202947_16_ITEM8_P18_S1	The Company does not record a receivable for recoveries from third parties for environmental matters until it has determined that the amount of the collection is reasonably assured.
202947_16_ITEM8_P18_S2	The accrued liability is relieved when the Company pays the liability or a third party assumes the liability.
202947_16_ITEM8_P18_S3	Upon determination that collection is reasonably assured or a third party assumes the liability, the Company records the amount as a reduction of expense.
202947_16_ITEM8_P19_S0	The Company charges to expense those costs that do not extend the life, increase the capacity or improve the safety or efficiency of the property owned or used by the Company.
202947_16_ITEM8_P20_S0	Revenues: Leasing The Company s properties leased to others are under operating leases.
202947_16_ITEM8_P20_S1	The Company reports leasing revenue when earned under the operating method.
202947_16_ITEM8_P20_S2	Certain of the Company s long-term land leases, including the outdoor advertising locations, provide for presently known scheduled rent increases over the remaining terms (30 to 138 years).
202947_16_ITEM8_P20_S3	The Company follows GAAP in accounting for leases by recognizing leasing revenue on the straight-line basis over the terms of the leases; however, the Company does not report as revenue that portion of such straight-line rentals which management is unable to conclude is realizable (collectible) due to the length of the lease terms and other related uncertainties.
202947_16_ITEM8_P21_S0	Petroleum storage facility The Company reports revenue from the operations of the Facility when earned and reports as revenue the tenant s portion of the real property taxes and certain other items as required by the lease.
202947_16_ITEM8_P21_S1	Contingent The Company reports contingent revenue in the period in which the factors occur on which the contingent payments are predicated.
202947_16_ITEM8_P22_S0	Income taxes: The Company and its subsidiaries file consolidated income tax returns.
202947_16_ITEM8_P22_S1	The Company provides for income taxes based on income reported for financial reporting purposes.
202947_16_ITEM8_P22_S2	The provision for income taxes differs from the amounts currently payable because of temporary differences associated with the recognition of certain income and expense items for financial reporting and tax reporting purposes.
202947_16_ITEM8_P22_S3	The Company follows GAAP in accounting for uncertainty in income taxes.

202947_16_ITEM8_P42_S0	The Pier is a deep-water pier in East Providence, Rhode Island owned by the Company which is integral to the operation of the Terminal.

202947_16_ITEM8_P43_S0	Environmental incident (2002): In 2002, during testing of monitoring wells at the Terminal, the Company s consulting engineer discovered free floating phase product in a groundwater monitoring well located on that portion of the Terminal purchased in 2000.
202947_16_ITEM8_P43_S1	Laboratory analysis indicated that the product was gasoline, which is not a product the Company ever stored at the Terminal.
202947_16_ITEM8_P43_S2	The Company commenced an environmental investigation and analysis, the results of which indicate that the gasoline did not come from the Terminal.
202947_16_ITEM8_P43_S3	The Company notified the Rhode Island Department of Environmental Management ( RIDEM ).
202947_16_ITEM8_P43_S4	RIDEM subsequently identified Power Test Realty Partnership ( Power Test ), the owner of an adjacent parcel, as a potentially responsible party for the contamination.
202947_16_ITEM8_P43_S5	Getty Properties Corp. is the general partner of Power Test.
202947_16_ITEM8_P44_S0	Power Test challenged that determination and, after an administrative hearing, in October 2008 a RIDEM Hearing Officer determined that Power Test is responsible for the discharge of the petroleum product under the Rhode Island Oil Pollution Control Act, R.I.G.L. Section 46-12.5.1-3 and Rule 6(a) and 12(b) of the Oil Pollution Control Regulations.
202947_16_ITEM8_P44_S1	The RIDEM Decision and Order requires Power Test to remediate the contamination as directed by RIDEM and remanded the proposed penalty to RIDEM for recalculation.
202947_16_ITEM8_P44_S2	In November 2008, Power Test appealed the decision to the Rhode Island Superior Court.
202947_16_ITEM8_P44_S3	In addition, in November 2008, Power Test sought, and received, a stay of the Decision and Order of the Hearing Officer pending a clarification by RIDEM of the amount of the proposed penalty.
202947_16_ITEM8_P44_S4	In October 2009, RIDEM issued a recalculated administrative penalty, and, subsequently, the RIDEM Hearing Officer issued a recommended amended decision, which was affirmed as a final decision by the RIDEM Director in December 2009.
202947_16_ITEM8_P44_S5	In January 2010, Power Test appealed that decision to the Superior Court.
202947_16_ITEM8_P44_S6	In September 2011, the Superior Court affirmed the decision of the RIDEM director.
202947_16_ITEM8_P44_S7	Power Test has appealed that decision to the Rhode Island Supreme Court.
202947_16_ITEM8_P44_S8	On March 4, 2016, the Supreme Court affirmed the decision of the Superior Court and the 2009 decision of the RIDEM Director.
202947_16_ITEM8_P45_S0	In April 2009, the Company sued Power Test and Getty Properties Corp. in the Rhode Island Superior Court seeking remediation of the site or, in the alternative, the cost of the remediation.
202947_16_ITEM8_P45_S1	On May 1, 2009, Power Test and Getty Properties Corp. removed the action to the United States District Court for the District of Rhode Island ( the Court ).
202947_16_ITEM8_P46_S0	On May 22, 2009, Power Test and Getty Properties Corp. answered the Complaint and filed a Counterclaim against Dunellen, LLC and Capital Terminal Company alleging that Dunellen, LLC and Capital Terminal Company are responsible for the contamination.
202947_16_ITEM8_P46_S1	Getty Properties Corp. and Power Test joined Getty Petroleum Marketing, Inc., the tenant under a long-term lease with Getty Properties Corp. of the adjacent property, as a defendant.
202947_16_ITEM8_P46_S2	The Company amended its Complaint to add Getty Petroleum Marketing, Inc. as a defendant.
202947_16_ITEM8_P46_S3	Getty Petroleum Marketing, Inc. moved for summary judgment against the Company, Getty Properties Corp. and Power Test.
202947_16_ITEM8_P47_S0	On December 5, 2011, Getty Petroleum Marketing, Inc. filed for bankruptcy under Chapter 11 of the United States Bankruptcy Act.
202947_16_ITEM8_P47_S1	Thereafter, with Bankruptcy Court approval, Getty Petroleum Marketing, Inc. rejected its lease with Getty Properties Corp.
202947_16_ITEM8_P47_S2	On August 24, 2012, the Bankruptcy Court approved a plan to liquidate Getty Petroleum Marketing, Inc.
202947_16_ITEM8_P47_S3	On January 15, 2013, the Court granted Getty Petroleum Marketing, Inc. s motion for summary judgment against the Company, Getty Properties Corp. and Power Test, dismissing the Company s third-party complaint.
202947_16_ITEM8_P47_S4	The parties have agreed to stay the litigation pending a determination by the Rhode Island Supreme Court on the Power Test appeal.
202947_16_ITEM8_P47_S5	The Company is evaluating its position in light of the decision of the Supreme Court referred to above.
202947_16_ITEM8_P47_S6	Since January 2003, the Company has not incurred significant costs in connection with this matter, other than ongoing litigation costs, and is unable to determine the costs it might incur to remedy the situation, as well as any costs to investigate, defend and seek reimbursement from the responsible party with respect to this contamination.
202947_16_ITEM8_P48_S0	In 1994, a leak was discovered in a 25,000 barrel storage tank at the Terminal which allowed the escape of a small amount of fuel oil.
202947_16_ITEM8_P48_S1	All required notices were made to RIDEM.
202947_16_ITEM8_P48_S2	In 2000, the tank was demolished and testing of the groundwater indicated that there was no large pooling of contaminants.
202947_16_ITEM8_P49_S0	In 2001, RIDEM approved a plan pursuant to which the Company installed a passive system consisting of three wells and commenced monitoring the wells.
202947_16_ITEM8_P49_S1	In 2003, RIDEM decided that the passive monitoring system previously approved was not sufficient and required the Company to design an active remediation system for the removal of product from the contaminated site.
202947_16_ITEM8_P49_S2	The Company and its consulting engineers began the pre-design testing of the site in the fourth quarter of 2004.
202947_16_ITEM8_P49_S3	The consulting engineers estimated a total cost of $200,000 to design, install and operate the system, which amount was accrued in 2004.
202947_16_ITEM8_P49_S4	Through 2006, the Company had expended $119,000 and has not incurred any significant costs since then.
202947_16_ITEM8_P50_S0	the abutters of the proposed remediation system even though RIDEM has not yet taken any action on the Company s proposed plan.
202947_16_ITEM8_P51_S0	As designed, the system will pump out the contaminants which will be disposed of in compliance with applicable regulations.
202947_16_ITEM8_P51_S1	After a period of time, the groundwater will be tested to determine if sufficient contaminants have been removed.
202947_16_ITEM8_P51_S2	In 2014, the Company engaged new consultants to work with RIDEM to develop the next phase of the approval process.
202947_16_ITEM8_P51_S3	While the Company and its consulting engineers believe that the proposed active remediation system will correct the situation, it is possible that RIDEM could require the Company to expand remediation efforts, which could result in the Company incurring costs in excess of the remaining accrual of $79,000.
202947_16_ITEM8_P52_S0	Income taxes: In 2014, Rhode Island changed the tax rate for corporate taxpayers from 9 percent to 7 percent effective January 1, 2015.
202947_16_ITEM8_P52_S1	The Company failed to adjust its deferred tax liability as reported in its consolidated financial statements for December 31, 2014 to reflect the downward adjustment in the rate.
202947_16_ITEM8_P52_S2	Had the Company properly reflected the rate adjustment, it would have reported a decrease of the deferred tax liability and an increase in shareholders equity, the deferred tax benefit and net income of $163,000.
202947_16_ITEM8_P52_S3	The adjustment would have increased basic income per share by $0.02.
202947_16_ITEM8_P52_S4	The Company has determined that the effect of this error in its consolidated financial statements at and for the year ended December 31, 2014 was not material.
202947_16_ITEM8_P52_S5	The Company recorded the adjustment in its consolidated financial statements for the year ended December 31, 2015, which decreased the deferred tax liability and increased shareholders equity, the deferred tax benefit and net income by $163,000 and its effective tax rate from 39 percent to 34 percent.
202947_16_ITEM8_P52_S6	The effective tax rate in the quarterly consolidated financial statements would have been similarly affected.

202947_16_ITEM9A_P1_S0	The Company s management is responsible for establishing and maintaining adequate internal control over financial reporting (as such term is defined in Rules 13a-15(f) and 15d-15(f) under the Exchange Act).
202947_16_ITEM9A_P1_S1	The Company s internal control over financial reporting is designed to provide reasonable assurance regarding the reliability of its financial reporting and the preparation of published financial statements in accordance with United States generally accepted accounting principles.
202947_16_ITEM9A_P1_S2	However, because of its inherent limitations, internal control over financial reporting may not prevent or detect misstatements.
202947_16_ITEM9A_P1_S3	Therefore, even those systems determined to be effective can provide only reasonable assurance with respect to financial statement preparation and presentation.
202947_16_ITEM9A_P1_S4	Also, projections of any evaluation of effectiveness to future periods are subject to the risk that controls may become inadequate because of changes in conditions, or the degree of compliance with policies may deteriorate.
202947_16_ITEM9A_P2_S0	Management conducted its evaluation of the effectiveness of its internal control over financial reporting based on the framework in 2013 Internal Control-Integrated Framework issued by the Committee of Sponsoring Organizations of the Treadway Commission ( COSO ) as of December 31, 2015.
202947_16_ITEM9A_P3_S0	During 2015, the Company did not properly reflect the decrease of the Rhode Island corporate tax rate into its calculation of the deferred tax liability in its consolidated financial statements for the years ended December 31, 2014 or 2015.
202947_16_ITEM9A_P3_S1	The Company utilizes a third-party professional firm to review the tax provision as a control over the accuracy of the tax calculation; however, the control did not detect the error.
202947_16_ITEM9A_P3_S2	The Company has evaluated this control deficiency using guidance issued by the Securities and Exchange Commission and the Public Company Accounting Oversight Board and determined it was a significant deficiency.
202947_16_ITEM9A_P3_S3	The Company has revised the control procedure applied by the third-party professional firm to include a second level of review.
202947_16_ITEM9A_P3_S4	Based on this assessment, the principal executive officer and principal financial officer believe that as of December 31, 2015, the Company s internal control over financial reporting was effective based on criteria set forth by COSO in 2013 Internal Control-Integrated Framework.

202947_16_ITEM9A_P3_S6	Management s report was not subject to attestation by the Company s independent registered public accounting firm pursuant to rules of the Securities and Exchange Commission that permit the Company to provide only management s report in this annual report.

202947_17_ITEM1_P0_S0	Organizational History The Company was organized as a business corporation under the laws of Rhode Island in 1983 as Providence and Worcester Company and is the successor by merger in 1983 to a corporation also named Providence and Worcester Company which was organized under the laws of Delaware in 1979.
202947_17_ITEM1_P0_S1	In 1984, the Company s name was changed to Capital Properties, Inc.
202947_17_ITEM1_P1_S0	Segments Prior to December 20, 2016, the Company operated in two segments: leasing and petroleum storage.
202947_17_ITEM1_P2_S0	On December 20, 2016, the Company s Board of Directors authorized the sale of the Company s petroleum storage facility and related assets to Sprague Operating Resources, LLC, a subsidiary of Sprague Resources LP (collectively referred to as Sprague ), for a purchase price of $23 Million (subject to certain adjustments) resulting in the petroleum storage business (the Petroleum Segment ) being classified as discontinued operations for all periods presented.
202947_17_ITEM1_P2_S1	On January 24, 2017, the Company entered into a definitive purchase and sale agreement with Sprague (the Sale Agreement ) and the transaction was consummated on February 10, 2017.
202947_17_ITEM1_P2_S2	See Notes 9 and 10 to the Consolidated Financial Statements for further discussion.
202947_17_ITEM1_P3_S0	The Board s decision to authorize the sale of the Petroleum Segment to Sprague, which has been exclusively leasing the petroleum storage facility and related assets since May 1, 2014, was partly based on an evaluation of the Petroleum Segment s economic future as solely a distillate terminal and the significant capital investment and substantial risk related to converting a significant portion of the petroleum storage facility to gasoline in order to increase revenue.
202947_17_ITEM1_P3_S1	The Board concluded that a sale to Sprague was in the best interest of the Company s shareholders.
202947_17_ITEM1_P3_S2	As a result of the sale of its petroleum storage and related assets, the Company s operations are limited to leasing its real estate interests.
202947_17_ITEM1_P4_S0	The Company s principal business is the leasing of Company-owned land in the Capital Center area ( Capital Center ) in downtown Providence, Rhode Island under long-term ground leases.
202947_17_ITEM1_P4_S1	The Company owns approximately 18 acres in the Capital Center consisting of 13 individual parcels.
202947_17_ITEM1_P5_S0	The Capital Center (approximately 77 acres of land) is the result of a development project undertaken by the State of Rhode Island, the City of Providence, the National Railroad Passenger Corporation ( Amtrak ) and the Company during the 1980 s in which two rivers, the Moshassuck and the Woonasquatucket, were moved, Amtrak s Northeast Corridor rail line was relocated, a new Amtrak/commuter railroad station was constructed and significant public improvements were made to improve pedestrian and vehicular traffic in the area.
202947_17_ITEM1_P5_S1	With the exception of the Steeple Street property (see Parcel 20 defined below), the Company has not acted, and does not intend to act, as a developer with respect to any improvements constructed on Company-owned parcels.
202947_17_ITEM1_P5_S2	Rather, the Company offers individual parcels for lease pursuant to long-term ground leases with terms of 99 years or more.
202947_17_ITEM1_P6_S0	Each lease contains provisions permitting the tenant to develop the parcel under certain terms and conditions.
202947_17_ITEM1_P6_S1	Each lease provides for periodic rent adjustments of various kinds.
202947_17_ITEM1_P7_S0	Under the leases, the tenants are responsible for insuring the Company against various hazards and events.
202947_17_ITEM1_P7_S1	Each tenant is required to indemnify the Company with respect to all of the tenant s activities on the land.
202947_17_ITEM1_P7_S2	The leases contain other terms and conditions customary to such instruments.
202947_17_ITEM1_P8_S0	The Company first began offering parcels for lease in the Capital Center area in the late 1980 s.
202947_17_ITEM1_P8_S1	As of December 31, 2016, nine parcels have been leased by the Company under long-term leases of 99 years or more.
202947_17_ITEM1_P8_S2	Of the nine parcels, eight have improvements constructed thereon or under construction as follows:
202947_17_ITEM1_P9_S0	While seeking developers, the Company also leases Parcels 3E, 3W, 4E and 4W in the Capital Center area for public parking purposes on a short-term basis to Metropark, Ltd.
202947_17_ITEM1_P10_S0	Parcel 20 Adjacent to the Capital Center Since the 1980 s, the Company has owned an undeveloped parcel of land adjacent to the Capital Center, which is leased out for public parking purposes on a short-term basis.
202947_17_ITEM1_P10_S1	In 2007, the Company purchased the adjacent parcel containing a three/four-story 18,000 square foot building (the Steeple Street Building ) and related land for $2,329,000, which, together with the previously-owned land, now comprises Parcel 20, containing 26,600 square feet.
202947_17_ITEM1_P10_S2	The Steeple Street Building is on the State Registry of Historic Buildings.
202947_17_ITEM1_P11_S0	During 2010-2011, the Company substantially rehabilitated the Steeple Street Building.
202947_17_ITEM1_P12_S0	The Steeple Street Building has three commercial tenants with additional space available for lease.
202947_17_ITEM1_P12_S1	All of the properties described above are shown on a map contained in Exhibit 20.

202947_17_ITEM1_P13_S1	All but one of these locations are controlled by the Company through permanent easements granted to the Company pursuant to an agreement between the Company and Providence Worcester Railroad Company ( Railroad the remaining location is leased by the Company from a third party with a remaining term of three years.
202947_17_ITEM1_P13_S2	Although no new locations have been added since 2002, in 2013 Lamar converted billboards at two locations to electronic boards, which conversions extended the term of the lease for a total of twelve years to 2045.
202947_17_ITEM1_P13_S3	Lamar has a right of first refusal for additional billboard location sites acquired by the Company in New England and Metropolitan New York City.
202947_17_ITEM1_P13_S4	The lease with Lamar provides, among other things, for the following: (1) the base rent increases annually at the rate of 2.75% for each leased billboard location commencing June 1, 2006 and on each June 1 thereafter; and (2) in addition to base rent, for each 12-month period commencing each June 1, Lamar must pay to the Company 30% of the gross revenues from each standard billboard and 20% of the gross revenues from each electronic billboard for such 12-month period, reduced by the sum of (a) commissions paid to third parties and (b) the base monthly rent for each leased billboard display for such 12-month period.
202947_17_ITEM1_P13_S5	The Lamar lease contains other terms and conditions customary to such instruments.
